China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Purchase All Vessels of the Chekiang River Company; Nine Riverboats for a Price of 1.2 Million Yuan

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company only had one riverboat, the "Emei," for its Sichuan River route. Since the ship was wrecked two years ago, the company's Sichuan River liner service has been suspended for more than a year and a half. Currently, the "Emei" requires a long time and more than 100,000 yuan to repair, making resumption of service uncertain. However, in terms of business, it cannot remain closed for long and abandon the route. The company has held many meetings on this matter and decided to seek additional ships other than the "Emei" to resume service and restore the Yangtze River's upper reaches navigation in the short term.

Chekiang River Company Vessels for Sale

The American-owned Chekiang River Steamship Company originally joined American capital to build new ships and expand its operations. Its routes specialized in the Sichuan River section of the upper Yangtze River. Initially, it only had the Yichang-Chongqing route, but later it added riverboats and extended its routes. The direct Chongqing-Shanghai ships were first created by this company. Since the dissolution of the Seven Company Alliance last year, river freight rates have plummeted, and business has declined. In addition, the Minsheng Company has obtained exclusive rights to the Sichuan River navigation business, making it even more difficult for the Chekiang River Company to maintain its position. Its crew members are all foreigners, and various expenses are much higher than those of other ships. The China Navigation Cooperation Society will soon be established, making it difficult for foreign commercial ships to survive in China. The company's shareholders have agreed to sell all the ships and transfer the business to Chinese management. Upon hearing this, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company contacted the company to discuss the purchase.

Agreed Total Ship Price

The Chekiang River Company's influence on the upper Yangtze River is second only to Minsheng. Its routes include the Shanghai-Yichang, Shanghai-Chongqing, and Yichang-Chongqing routes. It has a total of nine large Sichuan River boats and shallow-draft riverboats, including the "Qi Tai," "Qi Ping," "Qi Chun," "Yi An," "Yi Ping," and "Yi Feng." Most of them are the latest gasoline engine models, with new hulls and high speeds, and their construction costs are very high. All nine riverboats are to be sold to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for a price of only 1.2 million yuan. After several meetings, a draft purchase contract is being negotiated. The Chekiang River Company has already sent the registration forms for the hulls, tonnage, dimensions, hatchways, and construction dates of the nine riverboats to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for review. Once the draft contract is signed by both parties, the ships can be delivered on a scheduled date, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will raise funds to pay the American company.

Art Exhibition Pre-Exhibition Day 16; American Economic Mission Visited Yesterday

Yesterday was the 16th day of the Shanghai pre-exhibition of the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art. It will close in a week and be transported to England for exhibition from November of this year to March of next year. After the exhibition in England, the exhibits will be transported back and exhibited once in Nanjing, but not in Shanghai again. Therefore, many people in Shanghai, considering the opportunity rare, have been visiting enthusiastically in recent days. The news obtained yesterday is compiled as follows:

Economic Mission Visited

The American Economic Mission arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. Various circles in Shanghai specially established a reception office to take charge of reception matters. The reception office has contacted the exhibition and was granted free admission to show preferential treatment. It has received a reply from the association, approving the request. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, four members of the reception office accompanied the leader of the American Economic Mission, Forbes, Deputy Leader Carroll, Secretary Stoddart, Accountant Shiverley, and members Dillingham, Rogers, Le May, Hutchins, Wickham, Jones, Bixby, Condict, Minor, Daly, and Condie, a total of 20 people, to visit the exhibition. The person in charge of the association guided them through the exhibits. The mission highly praised the exhibition's orderly presentation of antiquities and admired the greatness of Chinese art and the superiority of Chinese culture. They expressed their gratitude for the free admission.

Working Day and Night to Photograph Exhibits

The association's exhibition this time has a total of more than 940 exhibits. A large portion of them have already been photographed. However, photographing antiquities is different from ordinary photography. The lighting and shooting time must be extremely accurate to capture every detail. Therefore, the number of photos taken each day is small. A portion of the exhibits are still being photographed day and night, striving to complete all the photography before the end of this month.

Private Antiquities Not Collected

The exhibits selected by the association for the London art exhibition have already been reviewed and decided. Antiquities privately owned will not be collected. Recently, someone wrote to the association, offering to transport their privately owned antiquities to England for exhibition. The association has replied one by one, declining the offer.

Gu Shusen Returned to Beijing Yesterday After Completing His Work

Gu Shusen, the permanent director of the association and director of the Ministry of Education, returned to Beijing yesterday morning. Gu is skilled in calligraphy and painting, and specializes in painting bamboo. Recently, he specially painted several bamboo and rock paintings in the association's office and gave them to the association's staff. Lei Zhen, the permanent director of the association, is scheduled to come to Shanghai from Beijing tomorrow. The explanations for the calligraphy and paintings written by the association have been published successively. The following is a summary of the exhibits from the last chapter of the explanation:

Summary of Calligraphy and Painting Exhibits

The calligraphy and painting exhibits this time are limited to the collections of the Palace Museum and the Antiquities Exhibition Hall. Although the various schools and masters listed above cannot be fully represented, the works of important artists from each school have been selected as much as possible. Viewers can also gain a general understanding of Chinese calligraphers and painters and their characteristics. Other items are either unique and unsuitable for traveling far, or of slightly lower quality and not worth listing indiscriminately, or have fragile paper and silk due to age and cannot be hung, or are long scrolls that are difficult to unfold. After careful consideration, the items recorded in this catalog were obtained. In total, there are six calligraphy and painting works from the Tang and Five Dynasties periods, fifty-six painting works from the Song Dynasty, forty-one calligraphy and painting works from the Yuan Dynasty, forty-three calligraphy and painting works from the Ming Dynasty, and twenty-nine calligraphy and painting works from the Qing Dynasty, totaling one hundred and seventy-five items. Although omissions are unavoidable, the system is reliable. This is what we hope viewers will be satisfied with. Furthermore, the methods of mounting Chinese calligraphy and painting are unique to various countries. If there is any damage, it can be repaired. Among them, technicians such as Tang Jie and Wu Wenyu are as famous as the calligraphers and painters themselves. The styles of mounting, such as scrolls and albums, are convenient for storage and exhibition and are also unique to various countries. This is also for the viewers' reference. For ease of reference, a summary of Chinese and Western calendars is listed below: The Han Dynasty is from 142 BC to 220 AD, the Three Kingdoms period is from 221 to 265 AD, the Jin to Sui Dynasties are from 268 to 617 AD, the Tang Dynasty is from 618 to 906 AD, the Five Dynasties period is from 907 to 959 AD, the Song Dynasty is from 960 to 1275 AD, the Yuan Dynasty is from 1276 to 1367 AD, the Ming Dynasty is from 1368 to 1643 AD, and the Qing Dynasty is from 1644 to 1911 AD.

Excessive Tax on Bidding Money; Du Yuesheng Visits Kong to Discuss Reduction; Tax of 7% Affects Business

According to the Ta Kung Pao, after the Ministry of Finance imposed a tax on exchange transactions, the Finance and Economic Committees of the Legislative Yuan reviewed the results and reduced the tax rate in one fell swoop. The Ministry of Finance believed that the tax rate was too low and would invisibly allow speculators to manipulate the market. Therefore, it re-proposed raising the tax rate, and the principle was approved by the Executive Yuan and sent back to the Legislative Yuan for review and reconsideration. It was decided to exempt securities from tax and change the bidding money from 6% to 7% per item. The ad valorem tax on yarn, cloth, grains, and flour was set at 3.5%. The Ministry of Finance has set July 1 as the implementation date. Due to the excessive tax on bidding money, the Shanghai Gold Exchange will be severely affected in the future. Therefore, the board of directors elected the current chairman, Du Yuesheng, to be responsible for requesting a reduction from the authorities. Du went to the Central Bank on the day before yesterday to meet with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, stating the difficulties and requesting Finance Minister Kong to consider the difficulties of businessmen and find a way to reduce the tax to ease the burden on businessmen.

Minquan Ship First Voyage to the Sichuan River; Yesterday's Reception for All Sectors to Visit

The Minsheng Company's Minquan ship sailing on the Sichuan River, as the first voyage to the Sichuan River, specially invited all sectors to visit at 2 pm yesterday. Shanghai Manager Zhang Shulin of the company and Zhou Hai, the owner of the Minquan ship, were warmly entertained, and it was quite a grand occasion.

The Egg Industry Follows Suit and Creates Commercial Acceptance Bills

After the silk industry initiated commercial acceptance bills, it has attracted the attention of the financial market. Now, it is learned that the Egg Industry Association of this city has also decided to follow suit, sending a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce for the record. The Chamber of Commerce has also replied, approving the request. The original letter is recorded below:

Egg Industry Letter

Respectfully,

It has been observed that commercial acceptance bills have been in use in various countries for a long time. Recently, the business market in our country has been sluggish, currency has tightened, and funds have been exhausted to meet the need. The municipal silk industry association, in view of this, initiated the creation and use of commercial acceptance bills in order to increase the limited capital. The method is ingenious and well-intentioned, and we are extremely pleased. This proposal has been approved by the ninth executive committee meeting of our association. In addition to notifying the industry, a corresponding letter is sent to your esteemed association for the record. Furthermore, the acceptance bill book used by our industry is planned to be purchased from the silk industry association. As for the financial sector, it is planned that colleagues will contact banks and money shops for dealings. This is also enclosed for your information.

Chamber of Commerce Reply

Respectfully,

On the 22nd of this month, we received your letter stating that your industry proposes to use commercial acceptance bills and plans to purchase the bill book from the silk industry association. As for the method of discount, it is planned that colleagues will contact banks and money shops for dealings. Please file this for the record, etc. Your industry, following the silk industry, uses commercial acceptance bills, which is sufficient to circulate finances and benefit commerce, and set the tone for other industries that have not yet followed suit. We are very pleased. In addition to approving the file for the record, a corresponding letter is hereby sent for your information.

Postal Service Notice: Regulations for Accepting and Delivering Airmail on the Beijing-Chongqing Route

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 126 states: The China National Aviation Corporation's special Beijing-Chongqing air service will commence on the 10th of this month, with intermediate stops at Jiujiang, Hankou, Yichang, and Wanxian. Flights will depart from Beijing every Wednesday at 6:30 AM, arriving in Ba County at 5:00 PM on the same day. Return flights will depart from Chongqing every Thursday at 8:00 AM, arriving in Beijing at 6:30 PM. Although this special Beijing-Chongqing service does not fly directly to Shanghai, mail from Ba County, Wanxian, and Yichang destined for Shanghai after the Chongqing-Hankou flight departs on Tuesdays will be transported to Beijing via the Thursday Chongqing-Beijing special flight for transfer to Shanghai. This is faster than the original Chongqing-Hankou-Hankou-Shanghai service, which arrived in Shanghai on Friday afternoons. Additionally, after the Shanghai-Hankou flight departs every Tuesday, mail from Shanghai destined for Jiujiang, Hankou, Wanxian, and Ba County will be sealed and dispatched by the bureau at 3:00 PM that afternoon, transported to Beijing via Special Express Train No. 302, and transferred to the special flight, which is also faster than the original flight that day. This notice is hereby issued for general information.

Open Letter from the Chinese Physical Society to the Nation: Concerning the Issue of Weights and Measures

The Chinese Physical Society addresses the nation regarding the issue of weights and measures: Recognizing that the current regulations governing weights and measures in our country contain inaccurate definitions and oversights in the standard system, and that the names of the units are plagued with problems, the society, in its capacity as an academic body, submitted a request to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education in October of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), asking them to convene a conference of academic experts to revise the regulations on weights and measures. Subsequently, the Executive Yuan convened a meeting in the capital on March 1st and 2nd of the 24th year of the Republic (1935) to review the names and definitions of units in the standard weights and measures system, and decided to convene a formal conference in mid-May of this year to revise the regulations. We believe that the issue of weights and measures is of profound and significant importance to science education, industry, national economy, and the people's livelihood, and that all Chinese people should pay close attention to it. Therefore, we are highlighting the main points and offering our humble opinions, hoping that our fellow countrymen will consider them. (1) The Reasons for the Society's Request to Revise the Weights and Measures Regulations: The reasons for the society's request can be divided into three aspects. (A) The definition of volume in the weights and measures regulations for the standard system is inaccurate. Due to historical changes, the current international metric system uses two standards for volume: one is the cubic decimeter, defined as the volume of a cube with sides of one decimeter; the other is the liter, defined as the volume occupied by one kilogram (kg) of pure water at its maximum density. The two definitions use different standards, and although their values are very close, they are not equal. The weights and measures regulations stipulate the "liter" as the unit of volume, calling it a "gong sheng" (公升, liter), and then state that it is equivalent to one cubic decimeter (cubic decimetro), effectively confusing two internationally recognized units that are different. Therefore, it should be revised. (B) Errors in the regulations regarding the weight standard in the weights and measures regulations: The basic units in the weights and measures system, besides length, should be "mass" rather than "weight." Regulations in all countries specify mass because "mass" and "weight" are two fundamentally different physical quantities. Mass represents the amount of matter contained in an object, and its value does not vary with the object's location. Weight represents the magnitude of the Earth's gravitational force on an object, and its value varies with the object's location. Therefore, weight should not be used as a basic unit. However, the weights and measures regulations in our country go against this principle and recognize weight as a basic unit. This is a significant error and should be revised. (C) The naming method adopted in the weights and measures regulations violates the most fundamental spirit of the international metric system, is cumbersome, and leads to many abuses. The most fundamental spirit of the international metric system lies in its use of the decimal system for all units and its completely rational naming method. The decimal system is self-explanatory, so we will only briefly discuss the naming method for comparison. The essence of the international metric system's naming is that each quantity has only one name for its unit. Multiples of ten, hundreds, etc., above this unit, or tenths, hundredths, etc., below it, are indicated by adding a corresponding prefix indicating the quantity to the unit name, without establishing a separate name. This is not like the English system with its foot, inch, pound, ounce, etc., or like our country's system with its li, zhang, chi, cun, jin, liang, qian, fen, etc. This is the simplest and most rational method and should be followed. It is also obvious that units of different quantities should not have the same name to avoid unnecessary misunderstandings. In contrast, the names of the units in the standard system defined in our country's weights and measures regulations all inherit the names of our country's old system, prefixed with the word "gong" (公, metric), such as "gong li" (公里, kilometer), "gong chi" (公尺, meter), "gong cun" (公寸, decimeter), "gong fen" (公分, centimeter), "gong jin" (公斤, kilogram), "gong liang" (公兩, hectogram), "gong qian" (公錢, decigram), "gong fen" (公分, centigram), etc. "Gong chi" and "gong jin" are clearly not equal to "chi" (尺, Chinese foot) and "jin" (斤, Chinese pound), but people often like to abbreviate and simplify, so they often shorten "gong chi" to "chi" or "gong jin" to "jin," which has significant consequences. The old system and the newly defined "market system" in our country are not decimal, while the standard system is a decimal system. Continuing to use the old names leads to "one gong chi" being equal to "three market chi," but "one gong li" is not equal to "three market li," and "one gong jin" is equal to "two market jin," but "one gong liang" is not equal to "two market liang." This alone is enough to show that there is no need to inherit the old names for the units of the standard system. Moreover, in our country's old unit names, all those without a specific name are named with "fen" (分), "li" (厘), "hao" (毫), etc. The original intention was to use "fen" for the first decimal place (i.e., "fen" being one-tenth), "li" for the second decimal place (i.e., "li" being one-hundredth), and so on. However, this is no longer the case under the new system. According to the new system, the "fen" in "gong mu" (公畝, are) is one-tenth of it, the "fen" in "gong chi" is one-hundredth of it, and the "fen" in "gong jin" is one-thousandth of it. As a result, the words "fen," "li," and "hao" have lost their original meaning and have no fixed value. In fact, our country's old names were created in an era when science was undeveloped, and no consideration was given to their application in science, which is understandable. Now, instead of seeking to create new names, we are merely imitating the old ones, leading to completely different things in science having to use the same name. For example, when saying that the mass of an object is one "gong fen," not only can its length be one "gong fen," but its cross-sectional area can also be one "gong fen," which is obviously confusing and inconvenient to use. (2) The Principles Followed by the Society When Defining the Terms for Various Units of Weights and Measures: As mentioned above, the names of the units in the standard system defined in our country's current weights and measures regulations are inappropriate. In the "Nomenclature of Physics" defined by our society, the naming of the various units of weights and measures is based entirely on the resolutions of the National Conference on Astronomy, Mathematics, and Physics convened by the Ministry of Education in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Here, at the risk of being verbose, we briefly present the naming principles below. (A) The names of the main units of length and mass are defined as follows: Meter for Meter, Gramme for Gram, Liter for Liter. (Recently, various parties have strongly advocated changing the translation of "sheng" (升) to "li" (立). The names of larger or smaller volume units can also be named according to paragraph (C) below. Our society can also agree to use the word "li.") (B) The nomenclature for large and small numbers is defined as follows: Shi (什) for ten times, Bai (佰) for one hundred times, Qian (仟) for one thousand times, Zhao (兆) for one million times, etc. Fen (分) for one-tenth, Li (厘) for one-hundredth, Hao (亳) for one-thousandth, and Zheng (徵) for one millionth (i.e., one-millionth of Zhao). (C) The names of auxiliary units larger or smaller than the main unit are all prefixed with the corresponding name of the large or small number, without establishing a separate name. For the sake of clarity, we have listed the names of the length and mass units proposed by our society below. (Table of Length Unit Names) Qian Mi (仟米) Kilomefre, Bai Mi (佰米) Hectometre, Shi Mi (什米) Decametre, Mi (米) Metre, Fen Mi (分米) Decimetre, Li Mi (釐米) Centimetre, Hao Mi (毫米) Millimetre. (Table of Mass Unit Names) Qian Ke (仟克) Kilogramme, Bai Ke (佰克) Mectogramme, Shi Ke (什克) Decagramme, Ke (克) Gramme, Fen Ke (分克) Decigramme, Li Ke (釐克) Centigramme, Hao Ke (毫克) Hilligramme.

Reading this table, it is clear that the naming scheme proposed by our society is clear and simple, and completely eliminates the drawbacks of the names defined in the current regulations. It also has the following advantages: (1) There is no need to create new characters or innovate old ones. (2) There is no case of one name or one sound being used for two purposes. (3) Only the name of the main unit needs to be understood, and the names of its larger or smaller auxiliary units are all named according to the same rule. (4) The names of the main units are already quite common in domestic science textbooks. (5) The naming of large and small numbers is consistent with the currently used meanings. (6) These three principles can be extended to other units of physics without establishing another system. These advantages are all facts that can be seen and heard by everyone. Our society does not need to repeat the discussion. (3) The Revision of Scientific Terminology Should Be Presided Over by National Academic Groups and Published by Government Agencies Responsible for Cultural Affairs: Today, with the development of science, the divisions of disciplines are becoming increasingly refined. Those who do not specialize in a certain subject can hardly grasp its full content. Therefore, the definition of scientific terms must be presided over by experts to avoid errors. Once the terms of each discipline have been carefully defined using reasonable methods, the agency that publishes them should be the Ministry of Education, which is responsible for cultural affairs. This is inevitable. The terms of two disciplines are often related to other disciplines. The terms of basic disciplines should be defined first, and then the terms of other specialized disciplines should be addressed. Disciplines with mutual relationships often have the same name, so they should be communicated and unified to avoid discrepancies. All of this work must rely on the Ministry of Education to broadly invite experts to discuss it together to achieve success. However, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, after defining the weights and measures regulations, also has plans to proceed with the definition of scientific terms. Our society believes that the names of the weights and measures units are already inappropriate and need to be revised, so we must specifically point out this meaning in order to allow other, more complex scientific terms to be defined through proper channels, so as to avoid future chaos and disputes. The Ministry of Education's National Institute for Compilation and Translation entrusted our society with reviewing the "Nomenclature of Physics," and our society accepted the commission and carefully reviewed it, all based on the above-mentioned principles. Other disciplines should also follow this correct path to achieve good results. However, it is important to note whether the academic group entrusted by the government to revise the terms of a certain discipline has the nature of representing the scientists of that discipline nationwide. If it does have this representativeness, then the government's entrustment is appropriate, and the terms reviewed by it will not be full of errors and become a laughingstock. In short, the need to revise the weights and measures regulations has been recognized by all parties. The revision plan created by our society is based on the drafts of physics nomenclature from previous years over the past twenty years, and the resolutions of the National Conference on Astronomy, Mathematics, and Physics. It is a summary of the opinions of scholars in our field, not just a draft or the opinions of a few people. Here, we have briefly described the above at the risk of being verbose, hoping to improve the weights and measures laws to correct the foundation of academia. Our society is not talented, but we are willing to work together with the people of the country to achieve this.

Student National Goods Association: Actively Preparing to Promote National Goods Week, Holding Sample Exhibitions in Different Regions, and Determining Preferential Measures for Students

The Student National Goods Promotion Federation, after holding the citywide student national goods pledge ceremony and exhibiting domestic student supplies on April 18th, is now actively promoting and sparing no effort in carrying out the various planned tasks. In addition to soliciting essays and holding mutual selections, and recruiting members to organize recruitment teams, it has recently been actively preparing to promote National Goods Week, hoping to practically connect producers and sellers to achieve the practical effect of promoting national goods. The details of the plan are as follows: (1) The association is holding National Goods Week to seek practical connections between producers and sellers, hoping to achieve practical results. (2) National Goods Week is tentatively scheduled to be held separately in the following regions, at least once in each region: (A) Pudong District, (B) Punan District, (C) Puxi District, (D) Pubei District, (E) Special District 1, (F) Special District 2. However, if necessary, the association may make other arrangements. (3) The duration of each National Goods Week is set at seven days, and the dates will be determined and announced by the association. (4) During National Goods Week, in addition to holding gatherings and ceremonies in selected locations by the association, the following events will be held on separate days: (A) Sample Exhibitions, (B) Famous Speakers, (C) Costume Lectures, (D) Radio Broadcasting and Promotion, (E) Other Promotional Activities. (5) During National Goods Week, factories or stores in each district that deal in national goods should have the following representations: (A) Factories should designate a place to clearly display their products and indicate preferential measures for students and members of the association. (B) Stores that exclusively sell national goods should display new national goods, especially those suitable for students, prominently during National Goods Week, indicating prices and discount measures. Stores that do not exclusively sell national goods should set up a "National Goods Section" and a "National Goods Showcase" to promote public awareness. (C) All schools holding letters of introduction from the association to purchase goods from factories should be given special preferential treatment. (6) The preferential measures and displayed goods of each factory and store must be genuine. If any fraud or counterfeiting is found, it will be published in the newspaper for reputational sanctions. (8) Matters not covered in these measures may be amended at any time.

The March and April Monthly Cup shooting competition of the Chinese Corps and Translation Corps of the International Business Group: The personnel of the four classes A, B, C, and D held the competition at the end of last month, and the results have been published in this newspaper. The early morning fog had not yet dissipated, and the light was sometimes bright and sometimes dark, so shooting was difficult to achieve satisfactory results. As for April, it was routinely awarded to Zhou Zhixing with 19 points. Vehicle Accidents Last Month

According to statistics from the Public Works Department Police Department, in March of this year, there were 829 vehicle accidents, including 287 causing injury, with 10 deaths, 490 causing property damage, and 52 causing injury and property damage. In terms of deaths and injuries, 204 pedestrians were slightly injured, 19 were seriously injured, and 8 died. 119 passengers and drivers were slightly injured, 10 were seriously injured, and 2 died. In terms of location, 33 people were injured and 1 died at intersections, and 319 people were injured and 9 died at other locations. In terms of age, 74 people aged 46 and under were injured, and 5 died. According to reports, there were 2,433 cases of vehicle violations, of which 749 were prosecuted. 1,985 rickshaw pullers were disciplined for violations. 62 cases of excessive horn use by cars were prosecuted.

Large Bomb Explosion: Confirming the Death of Five People

Wang Xiaoquan, a native of Haimen who lived at No. 87 Wan'an Road near the Dongyue Temple in Jiangwan and made a living pushing a small cart, found a bomb more than two feet long while fishing in a small creek there the day before yesterday evening. He took it home to test and throw it, and it exploded on the spot, killing five people. The details have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Zhu Bingwen, the local bailiff of Banliutu, reported to the local court for an autopsy. Inspector Li Caigui was dispatched by the court, along with the coroner, to the scene. The autopsy confirmed that Wang Xiaoquan (22 years old), Wang Limin (25 years old), Hou Zhiqing (59 years old), Cao Ximao (4 years old), and Wang Gendi (4 years old) had all died from the explosion. Some had their abdomens ruptured and intestines flowing out, some had their hands and feet blown off, and some had their heads damaged. The forms of death were varied, and the situation was extremely tragic. After the judge finished the autopsy, he instructed the local bailiff to hurry and notify the family members to quickly prepare the coffins.

Green Grass and Fragrant Yin, the Spirit of Heroes Lives On: The Tomb Hall of the Unknown Heroes Is Completed: The Construction of Bridges and the Arrangement of Gardens Are Underway, and the Completion of the Entire Project Is Not Far Off

The local association of this city and all sectors of society are commemorating the soldiers and civilians who died in the January 28th Shanghai War and specially established the Tomb of Unknown Heroes in Miaohang, Jiangwan. Since construction began in July of last year, more than half a year has passed. Now the tomb hall, tomb gate, and memorial monument have all been completed one after another. The construction of bridge projects and the arrangement of gardens are now being accelerated, and the overall completion is not far off. The Dagong News reporter has investigated and reported the details as follows.

Land for Construction After the January 28th Shanghai War in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), many soldiers and civilians in our country died. Afterwards, the local association of this city initiated the construction of the Tomb of Unknown Heroes, so that future generations can admire them. Initially, the five members of the Construction Committee, Hu Yunqiu, Du Chongyuan, Kui Yanfang, Zhang Gongquan, and Zhang Xiaoliang, were responsible for the preparations. The tomb site was selected in Miaohang Town, Jiangwan. Because the area belonged to Baoshan County, fellow villagers from Baoshan in Shanghai and local people voluntarily contacted the association and offered to donate more than 30 mu of tomb land. All parties considered that the area was located in a remote township with inconvenient transportation, so they initiated fundraising to build a road connecting Shanghai to the town, connecting Lingnan Road in Zhabei to the south and Dachang to the west. When collecting land, each mu was given back a land price of 100 yuan. By the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the road was completed. Regarding the construction expenses for all tomb roads, the local association initially allocated 10,000 yuan, and the remaining funds were raised from all sectors of society in Beijing and Shanghai, totaling more than 100,000 yuan. Shen Yi, Xue Cixin, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Yansong, Lin Kanghou, and Dong Dayou were added as construction committee members to assist in the work. Dong Dayou, an architect, was responsible for the voluntary design of the entire project. The road construction project required 20,000 yuan for land and more than 20,000 yuan for bridges along the way, with a total construction cost of more than 50,000 yuan. After the road was completed, construction of the tomb began in July of last year.

Tomb Inscription When the tomb base was started last year, an inscription for the Tomb of Unknown Heroes was written and placed inside the cornerstone for future reference. The original text reads: "In the January 28th War, countless soldiers of our army gave their lives, and countless civilians sacrificed themselves. Their names are unknown, which is truly regrettable, but the spirit of the nation rests on them. This year, the Shanghai Local Association established the Tomb of Unknown Heroes to comfort the loyal souls and encourage future generations. A committee of 13 members was formed to oversee the matter. The members were Hu Yunqiu, Kui Yanfang, Zhang Xiaoliang, Du Chongyuan, Shen Yi, Xue Cixin, Dong Dayou, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Yansong, Lin Kanghou, and Jia'ao. The longest resistance and the fiercest artillery fire were in Miaohang Town. The Baoshan gentry and people assisted with a donation of 33 mu, two fen, one li, two hao, and 1/10000 of a hao of land at No. 10 of the Ju Zi We. We asked our compatriots to collect donations to first build a road connecting to Lingnan Road to the south and Dachang Town to the west, and then build a tomb hall. In July of the 23rd year of the Republic, construction began with the selection of materials. The planner was the architect Dong Dayou, the contractor was the Jiu Ji Construction Company, and the cost of materials and labor was 66,672 yuan, one jiao, and two fen. The cornerstone was laid in November, and the inscription was written by the Mayor of Shanghai, Wu Tiecheng. Therefore, the origin is described and the drawings are hidden. As for the beginning and end of the tomb construction and the beautiful scenery of the garden, they will be recorded in writing at a later date. November, 23rd year of the Republic of China, recognized by Zhang Jia'ao of Baoshan, written by Shi Tongren."

Current Status of the Project Since the Tomb of Unknown Heroes began construction in July of last year, more than half a year has passed. The first to be completed were the tomb gate, the passage, the surrounding walls, the flagpole, the stone steps, the tombstone, and the stone coffin in the tomb (containing the clothes of the deceased). A small stream separates the entrance to the tomb from the tomb hall, so a bridge needs to be built. According to Shi Tongren of the Creation Committee, the tomb hall has now been completed. The stone steps in front of the hall are made of genuine domestic stone, and the stone steps around the hall are made of artificial stone, but the appearance is no different from real stone. The construction cost of the tomb hall is 67,000 yuan. Only the bridge project remains unfinished. The garden surrounding the tomb needs to be arranged in autumn and winter due to seasonal reasons before it can be completed. There is a small pool in the tomb hall to store the stone coffin. The memorial monument (i.e., the tombstone) is located in the hall, more than ten feet high, with the five characters "Tomb of Unknown Heroes" engraved on it. It has been requested that Chairman Chiang write the characters. The memorial inscription will be engraved after the completion. The funding has exceeded the initial budget by more than 20,000 yuan, and the unfinished project still requires 20,000 to 30,000 yuan.

Municipal Conference Resolution: Opening of the Old City Temple and Yu Garden; Yesterday, a Meeting of the Three Guilds Was Convened to Discuss and Await Separate Decisions Before Further Processing

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, for the purpose of opening the Yu Garden within the Nanshi Old City Temple to allow people of all countries to appreciate it, specifically ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to instruct the Sugar, Money, and Bean & Rice Guilds to comply, and also ordered all subordinate bureaus to assist in the handling. Yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau sent personnel to Cuixiu Hall to convene a joint meeting of relevant agencies and organizations. The following is a record of the information obtained by a reporter from the Industrial Society.

Municipal Conference Decides to Open

The Yu Garden within the Old City Temple in Nanshi City was originally private property owned by the Sugar, Money, and Bean & Rice Guilds. Internally, it is divided into the Dianchun Hall (Sugar Guild), the Inner Garden (Money Guild), and the Cuixiu Hall (Bean & Rice Guild). The pavilions, terraces, and buildings within these three gardens are scattered among each other, with winding paths and corridors that attract visitors. Each blade of grass and tree, the scenery is particularly elegant. Since its construction, it has been hundreds of years, but it has always been locked, excluding tourists. Now, Mayor Wu Tiecheng believes that the three gardens are often closed, depriving people of all countries of the opportunity to appreciate them. Now, for the purpose of providing for people to visit and for international publicity, he specifically raised the matter for discussion at the Municipal Conference this month. Subsequently, the conference decided that the Municipal Government should instruct the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to immediately instruct the authorities of the three guilds to comply, and designated the Social Affairs Bureau as the convener, and instructed subordinate bureaus to assist in the process. After receiving the order, the Social Affairs Bureau immediately instructed the three guilds and sent notices to the various bureaus, scheduling the first joint meeting to be held at Cuixiu Hall in the Old City Temple at 1:00 PM on the 23rd of this month (yesterday). Each guild was required to send representatives to participate, it was said.

Social Affairs Bureau Convenes Meeting Yesterday

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau specially sent Mr. Zhang Binghui of the Fourth Section to convene the first joint meeting of relevant agencies and organizations at Cuixiu Hall in the Old City Temple yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. The representatives who attended the meeting included Wang Guoxian of the Public Security Bureau, Lü Hailan of the Education Bureau, Zhang Zhengpu of the Health Bureau, Zhang Binghui, Sun Yongyi, and Dun Junshi of the Zhaobei Branch, Ni Zuwang of the Finance Bureau, Xiao Hechang of the Public Utilities Bureau, Shao Yuli of the Public Works Bureau, Yao Zhaojun of the Land Bureau, Zheng Zenan of the Sugar Guild, Zheng Zhou, Shen Wenhong of the Money Guild, and Gu Xinyi of the Bean & Rice Guild, totaling fourteen people. Zhang Binghui presided over the meeting, with Mr. Guo as the recorder. After performing the formalities, the chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting and the process of implementing the Municipal Government's instructions. Subsequently, the representatives of the three guilds expressed their opinions separately, as well as the difficulties in opening. The representatives of the various bureaus also successively explained their respective situations, as well as the future situation. Then, the discussion began on: (1) the original plan for opening; (2) the decision on the opening date. As a result of the discussion, it was decided that the representatives of the three guilds should first convene their respective trades to discuss the principles of opening, and then report the results of the meeting to the Social Affairs Bureau for further discussion before May 15. The meeting adjourned at about 5:00 PM after the discussion was completed.

The Public Works Department Will Begin Cholera Prevention Injections

The Public Works Department's Health Department will begin free cholera prevention injections starting May 1. Anyone who wishes to be injected can go to a nearby health sub-office or contact the medical officer on the injection car. Factory owners who wish to have a large number of workers injected can consult with the health sub-office or make an appointment by telephone. The distribution of time in each location is listed below: "Injection Car No. 1" Work Location: Monday, East District 6, 30 Songpan Road; Tuesday, East Districts 4 and 5, 311 Yangzhou Road; Wednesday morning, East District 3, 133 Zhoushan Road; Wednesday afternoon, East Districts 1 and 2, 80 Tongzhou Road; Thursday, North Districts 1 and 2, 130 Haining Road; Friday, North District 4, 270 North Fujian Road; Saturday, North District 3, 190 North Sichuan Road. "Injection Car No. 2" Work Location: Monday, West District 1, 260 Avenue Road; Tuesday, West District 2, 160 MacKenn Road; Wednesday, West District 3, 435 Robison Road; Sunday, West District 4, 1360 Yuyuan Road; Friday morning, Central District 2, 667 Fuzhou Road; Friday afternoon, Central District 3, same as above; Saturday, Central District 1, 340 Hankou Road.

Wusong Fishing Market Approaching; Three Fishing Firms Have Opened Their Doors to Await the Arrival of Boats

The annual fishing market season in Wusong is approaching. Currently, all fishing boats are opening their nets in the fish-producing waters to catch spring fish. If the weather is favorable, it is hoped that the boats will arrive within the next three to five days. If not, they will definitely arrive by the end of the month at the latest. Therefore, the three fishing firms in this port, namely Cuifeng (the firm name is Cuisheng), Baofeng, and Shentai, sent personnel with the necessary equipment to Wusong in the past two days to open their doors and await the arrival of the fishing boats. In addition, many guest merchants who make a living from the fishing season have also come to Wusong one after another, renting houses to live in and looking forward to the boats' arrival along the riverside every day. As a result, the Wusong market has suddenly become lively in recent days.

Siamese Travel Group Passes Through Shanghai; A Short Visit Ashore, Departing for Japan This Morning, and Returning to Shanghai via Tianjin in Two Months

A group of seventeen people from the Siamese Lower House Oriental Travel Group, led by Mr. Caiweier, Minister of Railways of the Kingdom of Siam, arrived in Shanghai at 4:00 PM yesterday on the President Coolidge of the Da Lai Company. They will continue to take the original ship to Japan tomorrow morning, then travel to Gulin in Korea and Northeast China. They will return to Shanghai in about two months for a longer visit. The details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

The Siamese Government Oriental Travel Group departed from Siam and made short sightseeing visits to the Philippines, Hong Kong, and other places along the way. The group consists of seventeen people, mostly members of the Siamese parliament. The leader is Mr. Caiweier, Minister of Railways of the Kingdom of Siam. The President Coolidge, which the group is traveling on, was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai the day before yesterday. However, due to fog along the way, the journey was delayed, and it did not arrive in port until about 4:00 PM yesterday.

Our Side Welcomes

Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Mayor Wu's representative Li Dachao, Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee representative Wu Gonghu, and others boarded the Da Lai Company's reception launch to the President Coolidge to welcome the group. They were greeted by Group Leader Caiweier. Li Dachao, Wu Gonghu, and others conveyed the government's welcome, in order to strengthen diplomatic ties. The group of seventeen then transferred to the reception launch and landed at the New Customs Wharf.

Group Leader's Remarks

According to Group Leader Caiweier, in an interview with reporters from various newspapers on the ship, the organization of this group is semi-official in nature. This time, they are going to Osaka, Japan, to participate in the Oriental Tourism Conference. They will make short sightseeing visits to the places they pass through. They arrived in Shanghai today and also plan to go ashore for a short stay. They will depart on the original ship for Osaka, Japan, tomorrow morning, where they will stay for four weeks. Then they will go to Korea and Northeast China, where they also plan to stay for one week each. From Northeast China, they will go to Beijing and visit for four or five days. From Beijing to Nanjing, they will stay for two days. From Nanjing, they will come to Shanghai again, at which time they will have a longer encounter with everyone, with a stay of about three or four days.

Group Members' Statements

The members of the group are all young, handsome, energetic, and friendly. According to the group members, the purpose of this trip is entirely for sightseeing. Although they do not have sufficient time to travel around China, they still hope to enjoy the beautiful scenery and new constructions in China in many ways and bring them back to their country as a reference. They also hope that this trip will further strengthen the friendship between China and Siam.

Denial of Anti-Chinese Sentiment

Regarding rumors that the Siamese authorities have an anti-Chinese sentiment and restrictions on the education of overseas Chinese in the country, the reporter asked Group Leader Caiweier about this. Caiweier was surprised to hear this. He said that Siam treats the overseas Chinese of any country equally, and that he had never heard of any anti-Chinese sentiment. Regarding education, there are no restrictions in the country. Whether this statement is reliable remains to be verified.

Departing for Japan This Morning

After landing at the New Customs Wharf, the group was led by Municipal Government representative Li Dachao and others on a short tour of the Bund and the main roads in the central district. In the evening, they hired a boat to return to the President Coolidge for the night. This morning at about 8:00 AM, the ship set sail for Osaka, Japan.

After the Easter Holiday, the Police Resolved More Than 300 Cases; More Than 300 Male Suspects and More Than 100 Female Suspects; The Highest Record of Cases Accepted by the First Special Court

From the 19th to the 22nd of this month, it was the Western Easter holiday, commonly known as "Foreign Qingming." The Public Works Department of the Shanghai Public Concession, as usual, stopped working, and the fourteen police stations under its jurisdiction also stopped handling cases for four days. Starting yesterday, the cases were handled as usual. Because the number of suspects apprehended by each police station was extremely large, the First Special District Court was extremely crowded. In addition to those in the courtroom, there were also many spectators, so each courtroom was overcrowded. Bailiffs maintained order, and many police guards directed vehicles outside the court gate. According to an investigation by the reporter, the cases handled by the fourteen police stations yesterday included 93 simple cases. Presiding Judge Yinghua of the Second Tribunal accepted 61 cases from police stations south of the Suzhou Creek, and Presiding Judge Ye Shengchao of the Fifth Tribunal accepted 32 cases from police stations north of the Suzhou Creek. They were prosecuted by police lawyers Zhang Shizhu and Jiang Baolian. There were 69 local cases, with 10 handled by President Feng Shide of the First Tribunal, 33 handled by Presiding Judge Jiang Shuzi of the Third Tribunal, and 26 handled by Presiding Judge Liu Yugui of the Eighth Tribunal. Police representative lawyers Wang Yaotang, Li Zhishan, and Qian Xunjiu were responsible for prosecution. The High Court's Second Branch accepted two counter-revolutionary cases, with lawyer Gan Jingxian representing the police. Presiding Judge Shen Yangzeng of the Ninth Tribunal accepted more than 140 cases of contraband, as well as dozens of cases of prostitutes soliciting customers without a license. In summary, the most numerous cases were theft, opium use, gambling, and fraud, totaling approximately 300 cases including contraband. The number of suspects apprehended was 327 males, including one Russian, 20 females, and more than 140 prostitutes. This is the highest record of cases accepted by the First Special District Court in recent times.

Inspector Hu Prevents Conflict; Chinese and French Police Arrest Each Other

Gang Zhen, the director of the Xuhui Police Station in western Shanghai, recently received an order from the director to inspect the area from the 22nd to the 24th of this month, drawing Police Chiefs Chong, Yu Fuyao, Pan Xuezen, Hou Dingyi, and Liu Gancheng, along with 27 police officers, on a daily basis. They rode in a transport truck to conduct the inspection. At about 11:00 AM, they were returning to the station in the same truck when, near the Damuqiao on Xujiahui Road, three officers, including French and Vietnamese Chinese police numbered 67, blocked the truck and refused to let it pass. Inspector Hu explained the purpose of the visit to the officer, who then called the police station for instructions. However, the chiefs and officers waited in the truck for a long time without a reply. Inspector Hu then ordered all the chiefs and officers to get out of the truck and walk across the bridge and turn into Xiexu Road in the Chinese area to return to the station (because the bridge was narrow and the truck could not pass). Unexpectedly, the French police officer pursued them aggressively, crossed the bridge to the south, and blocked their path. Fortunately, Inspector Hu and others tried their best to dissuade him, and no major disaster occurred. After the incident, Director Hong immediately reported to the director by phone and requested instructions for handling the matter.

Dredging Bureau's Large Dredger Enters Jiangnan Shipyard; Inspection of the Ship's External Shape Begins; Dredging of the Tongsah Shoal is Imminent

The world's largest dredger, ordered by the Dredging Bureau from the German Schichau Shipyard, arrived in Shanghai on the 14th of this month. The ship was moored at the bureau's factory wharf at Zhanghuabang. In the afternoon of the day before yesterday, it sailed to the Changmiao Jiangnan Shipyard to inspect the external shape and the bottom of the ship. It is said that the inspection will take about a week to complete. Then, it will sail to the Tongsah Shoal outside the Wusongkou to test its efficiency. Dredging of the Tongsah Shoal is imminent.

Detention Center of the Second Special District Court; Detainees Dig a Hole to Escape; Fortunately Discovered and Stopped

The detainees in the detention center of the Second Special District Court often disregard the law and cause disturbances. Although they have been transferred to the procuratorate for investigation and prosecution, the detainees still show no signs of repentance. On the night before last (the 21st), the detainees held in Special No. 1 in the West Compound dared to conspire to dismantle the iron bars on the window and dig a hole in an attempt to escape. The on-duty guard discovered and stopped them. One iron bar had been dismantled, two had been bent, and the hole had been dug. The three ringleaders were immediately taken out and chained, awaiting investigation and legal action.

Robbing a Shed and Shooting Someone

The poor state of society has led to a series of theft cases, which are too numerous to mention in the newspapers. We have never heard of bandits patronizing sheds and robbing them, but unexpectedly, a robbery and assault occurred in a shed on Zhonghua Xin Road in Zhabei the night before last, which is truly unprecedented. The details are recorded as follows: Jiang Tingfu (35 years old), a native of Yangzhou, lived with his wife, Jiang Fang (38 years old), in a shed on Zhonghua Xin Road. Jiang usually made a living pulling a rickshaw, while Fang worked in a factory. The couple worked hard and were barely able to make ends meet. On the second day of the lunar month, Jiang Tingfu received 12 yuan in society dues. It is not known how this was known to thugs, who mistakenly believed that Jiang Tingfu had some savings. At about 1:00 AM on the night before last, three bandits, each armed with a pistol, broke into Jiang's shed. The door of the shed was simple and collapsed at the first touch. At that time, the Jiangs were fast asleep and were startled awake by the noise. The bandits immediately grabbed Jiang Fang and demanded to know where the money was hidden. The woman realized that it was a robbery and screamed in terror. The bandits were angered by her cries and fired a shot, hitting the woman in the throat. The second shot hit her in the neck, and she immediately fell to the ground injured. Seeing that they had caused a major disaster, the bandits did not dare to rob and fled in a panic. After the bandits left, Jiang Tingfu went forward to check and saw his wife lying in a pool of blood, already dead. Fresh blood was still gushing from her neck and throat. Jiang could not help but wail loudly at the sight. The Tanziwan police learned of the incident and immediately ordered the police to search for the bandits in all directions, but to no avail. They then went to the scene of the incident to investigate. Yesterday morning, the local headman Wang Shaoting reported the case to the local court and requested an autopsy. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Li Caigui, accompanied by Coroner Yi Zhiming, arrived at the scene. The autopsy revealed that Jiang Fang had two gunshot wounds, and the trachea had been severed. It was determined that she died from the injuries. The coroner ordered that the body be collected by the family members, pending the arrest of the bandits for investigation.

Miscellaneous News About Commercial Ships: Yili Loses Its Engine Blade, Old Ning Shao Collides with Qi Han and E Dong, Yong Shun Collides with a Sailboat and Loses Lumber

Yili Loses Anchor

The Yili, which sails between Shanghai and Wenzhou, lost its engine blade on this trip from Wenzhou to Shanghai in the Wuli waters off Wenzhou. The ship was unable to move, and the reason is unknown. The shipowner was in a difficult situation and requested the Taizhou, which sails the same route, to tow it. The Taizhou then sailed from Haimen to the Huangmen waters (near Wuli) and towed the Yili from Huangmen back to Shanghai. The Yili Company reassembled all the machine blades, and the Taizhou also had to recognize the towing fee, so the losses were significant.

Ning Shao Damaged

When the Old Ning Shao of the Ning Shao Company was berthing at the pontoon dock of the Ning Shao Wharf in Hankou at 7:40 PM on the 19th of this month, the Qi Han and E Dong, two dispatch ships, were swept away by the turbulent water from upstream and drifted to that location. They violently collided with the bow of the Old Ning Shao, and the keel of the bow was immediately damaged. Wang Shunfu, the acting shipowner, immediately inspected the damage and found that the iron plate on the outside of the bow at a point fifteen feet above the thirteen-foot waterline was bent inward by about two feet. In addition to notifying the Ning Shao Warehouse in Hankou in writing and negotiating with the two dispatch ships, Ning Shao arrived in Shanghai yesterday, reported to the company, and sent a letter to the China Ship Insurance Association to wait for a commissioner to inspect the damage.

Yong Shun Collision

The Yong Shun of the Datong Xing Company, which sails the Shanghai-Beiyang route, was sailing from Longkou to Dengzhou at 7:30 AM on the 2nd of this month when it collided with the Zhang Zengshun's sailing boat near Lejiakou due to the dark weather. The sailboat was damaged and lost several pieces of lumber. Fortunately, none of the crew members were injured. The captain of the Yong Shun and the crew members of the sailboat went to the Dengzhou Customs to report the incident, and the Customs signed the report. The matter is still under negotiation, and the amount of the loss is unknown. According to a telephone call from the head office of the Zhengji Company, the company's Hui'an encountered a storm on the Beiyang route and took shelter, damaging a small boat belonging to Yuanchang. The loss was minor. According to a telegram from Yuanchang, the loss is estimated at 300 yuan, and negotiations are underway to claim compensation.

Using the Name of Opening a Carpet Company; Actually Manufacturing Drugs; Supervised by a Westerner's Houseboy; Master Finds Out and Reports to Police, Case Solved

Zhao Jianqiu, a native of Zhili, and Wang Huifang, Shen Juchuan, and others jointly established a drug manufacturing organization, hiring a certain engineer to be responsible for the manufacturing work and selling the drugs to various places. Later, due to a dispute over profit sharing between the engineer and Wang and Shen, they broke up. The engineer left without saying goodbye. Zhao and others were deeply afraid that the engineer would be detrimental to them, so they had to close down the business and move to a better location. Because they did not have a suitable location at the time, Zhao Jianqiu consulted with his fellow villager Wu Ruqing. Wu was a houseboy for Hagen, the manager of the electric power company at No. 17 Lusanne Road in the French Concession, so he agreed to temporarily store some of the drugs and equipment at Wu's place. Wu Ruqing then asked his friend Pan Genlin, also a native of Zhili, to find a solution. After several discussions, Pan, although he was also a houseboy for a Westerner at No. 11 Pushi Road in the French Concession, did not dare to store the rest of the drugs because he had not obtained the consent of his master. They then rented a house at No. 12 and a half next door. On the surface, it was to open a carpet company, but in reality, they were preparing to secretly manufacture and sell drugs. They appointed Zhao Jianqiu as the manager, so they had been busy cleaning the house and arranging the equipment in recent days. Just as they were preparing to choose an auspicious day to open, Wu Ruqing's secretive actions were discovered by his master, Hagen. On the afternoon of the 18th of this month, he called the Jing'an Temple police station and said that his houseboy Wu Ruqing had engaged in private drug manufacturing. He asked them to send detectives to investigate immediately. Upon receiving the report, the police chief immediately sent Chinese detective Shi En and Western detective Ma Ya to arrest Wu. They then went to No. 12 and a half Pushi Road and arrested Pan Genlin, Zhao Jianqiu, Liu Zhongxian, Li Deyuan, and the woman Zhao Wu, and seized manufacturing equipment, rubber tubes, test tubes, glass measuring instruments, 18 bottles of hydrochloric acid, empty coffee essence cans, and other items at the above two locations. They were all taken back to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu, in addition to prosecuting according to Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, also stated the facts of the case, saying that the main culprits Wang Huifang, Shen Juchuan, and others were still at large and had not been apprehended, so he requested a postponement. When questioned, the defendants, except for Li Deyuan, who said that he was a performer in the flying dance troupe on the rooftop garden of the Sincere Company, and Zhao Wu, who said that she was a prostitute who was hired by Zhao Jianying to accompany him, gave evasive answers. They also hired Wu Linkun and Fan Gang as lawyers to defend them. Presiding Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the confessions and ordered that the defendants be remanded in custody pending a new trial next Wednesday.

Aesop's Circus Has Already Opened

The entire English Aesop Circus arrived in Shanghai on the 18th, and immediately unloaded and landed, transporting everything to the theater across from the Great World. After three days of intensive preparations, it officially opened the night before last (the 21st). The audience was packed that evening, with every seat filled. There were a total of 21 programs, which were exciting and moving, far surpassing the Haikingber Circus from two years ago. The show is divided into two parts, with a ten-minute intermission in between. During the intermission, first-class and box seat viewers are free to visit the zoo without additional charge. There are four types of tickets: box seats are 4 yuan per person, first class is 3 yuan, second class is 2 yuan, third class is 1 yuan, and ordinary is 5 jiao. Seats can be reserved at the Muller & Phipps in Nanjing Road, or can be directly booked at the circus. The new phone number for the theater is 80196, for inquiries from all sectors. It is said that matinee performances will be added every Wednesday, Saturday, and Sunday, with tickets costing only half price to give preferential treatment to children.

Shanghai Gas Company to Implement New Price List on a Regular Basis, Starting May 1

In order to allow users to share in the benefits of the new gas plant, the Shanghai Gas Company has decided to implement a new price list starting May 1 of this year. This will enable the general users to benefit from this. The new price list is called the Dual Tariff Plan. The price of gas used for water heaters (including fountains), stoves, and boilers will be reduced by 21 percent. The previous price was 2 yuan and 8 jiao 5 fen per thousand cubic feet, but now it will only be 2 yuan and 1 jiao 5 fen. However, this benefit can only be enjoyed by those who use gas for cooking in addition to hot water. The regulations are as follows: (1) Gas used for cooking, hot water, and/or stoves will be equipped with separate meters for distinction. (2) The price of gas for cooking will still be calculated at 2 yuan and 8 jiao 5 fen per thousand cubic feet, and will not be changed. For those who use less than 900 cubic feet, the minimum price of 2 yuan and 5 jiao will still be charged. (3) Those who enjoy the benefit of 2 yuan and 2 jiao 5 fen per thousand cubic feet must use 3,500 cubic feet or more per month. (4) Under this new plan, there is no minimum consumption requirement for gas used for hot water and/or stoves. (5) Existing users who have cooking appliances and water heaters will not be charged extra for installing separate meters. If the new meter is not installed by May 1, the discount will be based on the reading of the newly installed meter. (6) Users who already have cooking appliances and install a separate water heater will be charged 10 yuan for installation. Users who already have a water heater and install a separate cooking appliance will be charged 7 yuan and 5 jiao for installation. The installation fee for each stove and boiler is 5 yuan.

Child Trafficking Case Cracked on the Hai'an Ship

The Water Police reported that they had received a telegram from the Wenzhou Public Security Bureau through Shi Weijun, the special commissioner of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, stating that the company's Hai'an ship, which had set sail from Wenzhou to Shanghai this time, had child traffickers who had abducted three young children and were on the ship. They requested that the police pay attention and send officers to investigate and arrest them. Upon receiving the report, the police chief immediately sent detectives Huang Zhenlin, Hu Changqing, and Liang Shenqing, along with Commissioner Shi, to wait at the wharf. It was not until 12:45 PM yesterday that the Hai'an ship arrived and docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf. The detectives immediately boarded the ship to investigate and found the traffickers Lin Chaogeng (also known as Lin A'gen, 40 years old, from Wenzhou) and Pan Taihuang (39 years old, from Wenzhou), as well as the three abducted boys Liang A'zeng (17 years old), Liu A'en (17 years old), and Lin A'liang (16 years old, all from Wenzhou) in the steerage. They were all taken to the police station. Yesterday afternoon, a letter was prepared and sent to the local court to transfer all the people. Prosecutor Li interrogated them and ordered that Lin and Pan be detained for further investigation. The victims Liang A'zeng and the other two boys were temporarily detained pending their families' arrival to claim them and be reunited.

Calligraphy Masterpieces by Zhong Yao and Cai Xiang Offered for Sale

In our country, the calligraphy of famous historical figures has always been regarded as a national treasure. Among all the world's written languages, Chinese characters, with each character representing a sound and standing independently, are unique. Other languages are formed using phonetic spellings. This is why Chinese characters are so precious. Zhong Yao (Yuan Chang), a figure from the Wei Dynasty, is considered to have created first-rate calligraphy in Chinese history. Zhong Yao and Wang (Xizhi) are always mentioned together. Zhong Yao's calligraphy is even more valuable than Wang Xizhi’s. Cai Xiang, styled Junmo, served as Shangshu during the reign of Emperor Shenzong of the Song Dynasty. His calligraphy has long been praised by the art world. The authentic works of such figures are rare treasures in our country, and all Chinese people should cherish them. A certain gentleman from Zhejiang Province, currently studying abroad, finds it difficult to protect such precious items due to the prevalence of bandits in his hometown. This is particularly true for calligraphy and paintings, which require even greater care. Currently, this gentleman has brought these two calligraphic works (authentic pieces by Zhong and Cai) to Shanghai and is willing to sell them. For the sake of preserving national treasures, he has rejected several offers from foreigners. If there are domestic collectors who love Chinese culture and can ensure their safekeeping, he is willing to sell them at a low price to prevent these national treasures from flowing abroad. These two pieces were originally Imperial Collection, later entering the household of a certain Prime Minister. Therefore, the scrolls bear the seals of the Eight Treasures and inscriptions by court historians. After the Republic of China was established, the Prime Minister's family declined, and their descendants sold these treasures. At that time, the gentleman's late father, who was living in Hangzhou, feared that these national treasures would fall into the hands of foreigners and be either transported abroad or ruined. Therefore, he purchased them at a high price and treasured them. Now that the gentleman's late father has passed away, he finds it difficult to protect them and has decided to sell them at a low price. Contact at No. 17 Jiaping Lane, Jiaozhou Road, Avenue Edward VII, Shanghai, between 4:30 PM and 5:30 PM daily.

The San Cai Cotton Weaving Company Opens on Schedule

The San Cai Cotton Weaving Company, located at the intersection of Zhonghua Road and Old West Gate in Nanshi, was founded by Gao Chengyuan and others with pooled capital. It produces its own cotton woven goods, promotes the sale of fine domestic products, and reportedly includes dozens of sections for towels, fabrics, bedsheets, clothing, socks, school supplies, household items, travel items, etc. Virtually everything needed for daily life is available. The grand opening is scheduled for April 26th in the Gregorian calendar. There will be large giveaways that change daily, aiming to provide customers with tangible benefits. In addition to the daily giveaways, the company will also offer special, attractively priced items to encourage customers to use domestic products. The company's motto is "Top quality, lowest price."

Hua De Factory's New Invention, the Silver Light Bulb, Sells Well

The Hua De Light Bulb Factory on Xian Road has invented a new type of silver light bulb, for which it has been granted a special patent by the Ministry of Industry. It is said that the bulb's manufacturing method is new and unique, saving electricity while being durable, and providing twice the brightness of ordinary light bulbs. Various electrical appliance stores in the city have them on display for sale. Some who have already tried them say that this type of silver light bulb is indeed superior to any other light bulb.

Kang Ji Grand Theater Presents the First Part of "Wu Song"

Since Kang Ji Grand Theater on Second Ma Road engaged the renowned Wusheng actor Gai Jiaotian to perform the first part of "Wu Song," his reputation has proven well-deserved, with exceptionally high attendance. It is said that the theater owner, Mr. Guo Quanjian, persistently invited Mr. Gai, who is nearing seventy, to perform in Shanghai. Unable to decline, Mr. Gai agreed to perform for ten days, after which he will retire to rest by West Lake. His son, Zhang Yipeng, will take over. Zhang Yipeng is a handsome young man with a strong family background in the arts. The Four Banks Joint Treasury Issues its 277th Reserve Report

The Four Banks Joint Treasury is jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks, and specializes in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. In accordance with the Treasury's issuance regulations, the issuance of banknotes is fully backed by reserves, with a minimum of 60% in cash reserves and a maximum of 40% in guaranteed reserves. A public announcement is made weekly, and the report is audited by the auditors of the four banks and accountants. The following is the 277th public announcement of the Shanghai Treasury, dated April 20, 1935. Total banknotes in circulation: 21,617,873 yuan. Total reserves: 21,617,873 yuan. Cash reserves: 18,429,973 yuan. Guaranteed reserves: 3,187,900 yuan.

Weather Report

The Zikawei Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, stating that the area around Shandong is cloudy but mostly clear, with strong winds from the southeast to southwest, due to a low-pressure system passing through southern Mongolia and moving eastward. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are changing from overcast to cloudy with fog, with gentle winds from the northeast to southeast. The East China Sea is overcast with localized rain, with winds from the northeast to northwest. Between the Ogasawara Islands and the Ryukyu Islands, there are cyclones and rain. The Taiwan Strait is cloudy but clear with fog, with variable winds. Furthermore, the highest temperature in the city within the 24 hours preceding 3:00 PM yesterday was 69.3 degrees, and the lowest was 55.8 degrees. The highest temperature on the same day last year was 63.9 degrees, and the lowest was 59.0 degrees.

Educational News

Jiangsu Province Implements Military-National Education, Selects Several Counties to Pilot Training of Strong Young Men First

In order to implement military-national education, the Jiangsu provincial authorities have stipulated that counties complete the first step of training township and baojia chiefs, and the second step is to implement the training of strong young men. After consultation between the Civil Affairs Department and the Security Department on the methods for training strong young men, it is reported that the provincial government meeting has passed it, and several counties will be selected to pilot it in the near future. The training period has been changed from three months to two months. The number of people is determined according to the needs of each county. In terms of military subjects, the Security Department will select knowledgeable personnel to serve as instructors. In terms of political training, commissioners will be sent from each district commissioner's office. After the training period is completed, there will be an obligation to serve the local area for a considerable period. The department will send personnel to review and assess their training achievements. The training of township and baojia chiefs in various districts in Jiangbei has already begun, and the progress is good. Several counties in Jiangnan have reported the completion of baojia handling. The entire process can be completed by the end of May. Currently, the Township Chief Training Preparatory Committee is compiling training materials. In the future, due to the large number of people (approximately 3,000), the training steps may be carried out in phases.

The Jiangsu Education Department Revises Audit Personnel Regulations, Cannot Self-Investigate Own Accounts, Explanation Requested by Ji Sui, Member of the Audit Committee of Jiangdu, Instructions for Compliance by Subordinate County Bureaus Issued by the Education Department

The accounts of various counties, schools, and social education institutions in Jiangsu Province are reviewed by the District Education Fee Committee. Responsible personnel are required to recuse themselves. Since the merger of the District Committee into the County Education Fee Audit Committee last year, the facts of self-reporting and self-investigation by attending representatives have been discovered. Bao Sui, a member of the Education Fee Audit Committee of Jiangdu County, felt that the above-mentioned conflict occurred, and specially requested the Jiangsu Education Department to issue an order for clarification. The Education Department believes that the representative should be temporarily excused when auditing the accounts of a certain representative. Recently, instructions for compliance have been issued to the 61 counties by the County Bureau.

The National Government Reviews and Approves the Education and Culture Funds for Jing and E provinces, Cities. The Submission of the 23rd Year Was Too Late, and Increased Efforts Should Be Made to Increase Them in the Future

The National Government recently issued orders to the various competent Yuan and Departments regarding the general budget of income and expenditure for the 23rd year of Nanjing Municipality and Hubei Province, which were passed by the Central Political Conference, dividing them into local general budgets, with the Nanjing Municipal Government divided into general and business categories, and also for temporary special funds, ordering the two provinces and cities of Jing and E to comply accordingly. Among them, regarding the education and culture funds, the 23rd year: (1) The regular expenditure of Nanjing Municipality was 965,476 yuan, compared to 854,968 yuan in the previous year, an increase of 20,508 yuan. The temporary expenditure for the current year was 472,000 yuan, compared to 192,800 yuan in the previous year, an increase of 179,200 yuan. (2) The regular expenditure of Hubei Province was 2,638,469 yuan, compared to 2,650,569 yuan in the previous year, a decrease of 2,200 yuan. The temporary expenditure for the current year was 262,045 yuan, compared to 8,056 yuan in the previous year, an increase of 253,989 yuan. In addition to ordering that the budget submission should be advanced in the future, so as not to repeat the late submission of the 23rd year budget that was more than half a year late, the National Government also ordered that the total of the education, culture, industrial, transportation, construction, and health expenses for the 13th year in E province accounted for only 28% of the total budget, and the education and culture expenses accounted for only 15%, which was too low. Article 15 of the Principles of the Financial Revenue and Expenditure System Law recently passed by the Central Political Conference has clearly stipulated that the minimum total amount of expenses related to education, culture, economic construction, health care, childcare, and relief shall not be less than 60% of the total budget of the province. This standard should be observed uniformly, and special attention should be paid to it when preparing the budget in the future.
