Municipal Education Bureau Sponsors Public Amateur Sports: Scheduled for May 26, Participation Instructions Issued

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau holds a public amateur sports meeting every year to promote public sports. This year is the sixth session, and it has been approved by the Municipal Government. It is scheduled to be held on May 26 (Sunday) at the Municipal First Public Sports Field. The participation instructions are disclosed as follows:

(1) Eligibility: Except for physical education teachers, school students, and members who scored points in the previous city-wide sports meeting, all citizens aged 18 or above are eligible to register.

(2) Sports Events: (A) Track and Field, (I) Men's Group: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1500 meters, 3000 meters, 100-meter low hurdles, high jump, long jump, triple jump, 5.438 kg (12 lb) shot put, pole vault, a total of twelve events. Each person can participate in up to three events. (II) Women's Group: 50 meters, 100 meters, baseball throw, high jump, long jump, a total of five events. Each person can participate in up to three events. If less than six people register for an event, the competition will not be held. (B) Chinese Martial Arts, (I) Men's Group: Boxing, Weapons, a total of two events. Each person may participate in all events, but only one routine is allowed per event. (II) Women's Group: The events and number of routines are the same as the men's group. However, if less than six people register for an event, it will be cancelled.

(3) Sports Meeting Date: May 26, starting at 8:00 AM. Participants must arrive at the field by 7:30 AM.

(4) Registration Dates: From May 5 to May 20.

(5) Sports Meeting Field and Registration Office: Municipal First Public Sports Field, Daji Road, Nanshi.

(7) Competition Rules: (A) Track and field will be conducted in accordance with the latest rules approved by the Chinese National Sports Advancement Association. The top five winners in each event will be awarded points: 5, 4, 3, 2, 1. (B) Chinese martial arts will be judged by the judges based on their level of skill. The top five performers in each event will be awarded prizes.

(B) Chinese martial arts athletes will be issued one number cloth each, to be pinned on the front of their chests. It must not be removed.

(9) Sports Equipment: Except for the bamboo pole for the pole vault and the weapons for Chinese martial arts, all sports equipment will be provided by the association.

Chi-Tse and Guanghua Middle Schools Win Right to Finals: Pudong Provincial Shanghai Middle School Competes for Final Spot Today

In the Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation basketball league, two games were played yesterday: (1) Chi-Tse defeated Guanghua 27-24; (2) Shanghai University defeated Fudan 46-24. Chi-Tse and Guanghua had both won all three of their previous games in Group C. Yesterday's match was essentially a battle for the right to the finals, and was therefore very important. No less than 200 male and female students from Guanghua came to cheer their team on. Chi-Tse had fewer supporters due to the long distance and difficult journey. The tension in the basketball court was no less than that of the Sino-American finals. Every basket was met with applause and cheers. As a result of the intense battle, Chi-Tse defeated Guanghua 27-24. The details of the first and second halves are as follows:

In the first half, under the command of A Pang Dai Changru, the two teams began to compete. Guanghua's right forward, Chen Bangben, was petite and lively. He shot from the left corner and scored first, to the thunderous applause of the Guanghua cheerleaders. Chi-Tse's players were all veterans of the arena and remained calm. Left forward Chen Yunfan took the opportunity to break through and lightly tried his hand, and sure enough, he scored, tying the score at 2-2. From then on, their momentum increased greatly, and they scored two more baskets, making it 6-2. Seeing that the situation was not good, Guanghua requested a timeout to calm their troops. In the ensuing battle, there were ups and downs. Fighting hard until the end of the first half, Chi-Tse led 17-12.

During the lemon break, Guanghua received instructions from their brain trust, Dong Xiaopei, and coach, Dong Jingnan. They showed great improvement after the start of the second half. The score gradually became closer and closer, from close to tied, and from tied to overtaking Chi-Tse. The atmosphere in the basketball court changed rapidly. At this critical moment, Chi-Tse's captain, Jiang Xuexin, immediately called a timeout to discuss a counter-attack strategy. However, after struggling until a minute before the end, Chi-Tse was still one point behind. Guard Xu Jianqing, seeing that time was running out, shouted and encouraged himself to move forward, broke through the siege, scored a basket, and took the lead by one point. Then Chen Yunfan took advantage of the situation to score another basket. The final buzzer sounded, and the fierce battle ended. As a result, Chi-Tse won the right to the finals by a score of 27-24. My Philosophy as a Basketball Referee (II)

— Authored by Mr. Dahl of the United States, Translated by Qian Yiqin

Immediate Judgment - In addition to the aforementioned, a referee must possess another crucial characteristic: the ability to render swift and accurate judgments on fouls. All fouls should be declared immediately; delays of several seconds are unacceptable. This does not imply anticipating fouls or declaring them an instant or seconds before they actually occur. Crucially, a foul must be established and clearly observed before the whistle is blown.

In other words, the referee's mind should not have time to ponder or debate the validity of a foul or whether it should be called. If a referee claims to arbitrarily enforce rules strictly or leniently, they undoubtedly commit the aforementioned error.

Related to this is a school of critics who argue, "Unintentional fouls or fouls far from the center of play can be ignored and not called." A certain newspaper review stated, "In the heat of a game, unintentional fouls by players are inevitable. If a referee insists on calling them, it is both unreasonable and lacks common sense." Another said, "Calling unintentional fouls far from the center of play unduly delays the game's progress. Should a referee then pause upon seeing a foul and debate whether it is a genuine foul, an intentional foul, far from the center of play, or committed by a team lagging behind in score? Should I then differentiate the declaration of fouls or execute it as is, or await closer competition before enforcing stricter penalties?"

A referee should never lightly relax during a game, regardless of how easy or one-sided it may seem, as tension can arise at any moment. If a referee hesitates or is unsure and questions whether a foul should be called, they will immediately lose the ability to manage the game and quickly find themselves in an awkward position. Once a referee loses control, trouble ensues and is difficult to recover from. At that point, misfortune arrives before the game is over or even concluded. In a one-sided game, never relax or show sympathy for the losing players by not calling their fouls. Fortune can be unpredictable; the struggle may quickly become close. If you have relaxed the rules for one side, the other will expect the same treatment, disrupting fairness and leading to immediate chaos. Relaxation by referees in one-sided games is a natural tendency, making them harder to officiate than close games, where referees are generally more cautious.

Consistent and Impartial Throughout - Another mistake referees must be particularly mindful of is becoming accustomed to anticipating an easy game. This is most likely to occur in a one-sided game when one team has a commanding lead. In reality, no game should be taken lightly. If a referee anticipates a certain outcome, the game may turn out the opposite, leading to a cascade of problems.

Furthermore, referees should not be concerned about one team committing more fouls than the other (whether in the first half or after the game). Referees should not check the record book during or after the first half to see the number of fouls they have called, or who committed them, as this may lead to attempting to equalize fouls in the second half.

Equalizing fouls between teams is something a referee must avoid at all costs, even if requested. If both teams have an equal number of fouls at the end of the game, that is simply a coincidence. In most games, it is natural for one team to commit more fouls than the other. The losing team may commit more fouls than the winning team due to aggressive defense and hasty actions. Smaller teams may commit more fouls than taller ones due to their tendency to grab, leading to fouls. However, taller teams may sometimes commit more fouls than smaller ones due to their tendency to push or surround opponents. If a foul is clearly committed, do not let the fact that one team is being penalized more affect your continued calling or punishment.

This raises the question: "How many fouls should be called in each game to be appropriate?" Even after discussion by hundreds of people, seeking an average number is futile. Therefore, any attempt to find an average number of fouls per game is highly questionable. Who can or, more importantly, who should dictate that? While reviewing last year's league records, I found two consecutive games particularly interesting, both officiated by the same two referees. In the first game, there were thirteen fouls, divided eight to five. In the second game, there were twenty-eight fouls, divided fifteen to thirteen. Why thirteen fouls in one game and twenty-eight in the other? Why dwell on such facts or even consider the reasons for the difference? The referees cannot create fouls, nor are they at fault for them. Whether there are ten, twenty, or thirty fouls, they are caused by the players and are not the referee's responsibility; they merely declare them.

Calling Too Many Fouls - A common criticism is that too many fouls are called during a game relative to its length, and that too many games are won by free throws. If twenty fouls are called for both teams combined (regardless of the level of play), that is one foul every two minutes of the game. If thirty fouls are called, that is one foul every minute, effectively halting the game half the time. However, considering the rapid pace of the game, such a ratio of fouls is not surprising.

Regarding the point that calling too many fouls delays the game, the answer can be "Yes" or "No," depending on the referee and their skills. One referee may call ten fouls and delay the game, while another may call thirty fouls and maintain a pace no slower than the one calling ten. My highest record is forty-eight fouls. I mention this not to boast about calling so many, but to highlight the fact that after the game, both teams commented on how quickly it was played and that no one, including the officials, realized so many fouls had been called. That game was a close encounter between two strong opponents. Readers should easily grasp the point.

Chronicles

Tidbits

— (Excerpt)

In ordinary letters, the writer's name is usually written at the end. Unsigned anonymous letters, logically speaking, should be called "tailless letters." However, people generally do not call them "tailless letters" but "headless letters." This is truly putting the cart before the horse!

Merchants selling goods, no matter what, always end up making some money. As the saying goes, "Sell a thousand, sell ten thousand, never sell at a loss." However, stores currently having clearance sales often use red paper with the words "regardless of cost." Furthermore, they often tell merchants, "This is a loss." If you are not considering the cost, then why not just give the goods away without taking any money? If it's a loss, then what is the point of making a profit?

On the one hand, accepting high praise from people, and on the other hand, also giving high praise to others. In this way, you neither wear other people's praise, nor do you give praise to others. Wouldn't that be refreshing! However, most people in the world are unwilling to do this. This is probably because they have deeply studied the philosophy of "eating, defecating, feces fertilizing the grains, grains then turning into feces."

Ah Xia

— Yixin

Ah Xia is the most lively of our colleagues. She has a beautiful face, charming eyes, and always walks with a twist. Especially when her clear singing voice comes from the music room, everyone feels like they've drunk a glass of rich wine.

But now Ah Xia has left here, and the time she left was so heartbreaking.

The fact is this:

Due to family financial reasons, she was betrothed by her despicable parents to Mr. Gu, who already has two children, since she was young. Naturally, she felt extreme pain, but what can she do? Opposing this unsatisfactory marriage is opposing the lives of her parents.

But she did not give up her youth. She needed a loyal lover, just as she needed life. She constantly cast sparks of her love towards people. Finally, her spark stopped with Mr. Gong. But she couldn't bear to lose her parents, losing their livelihood because of her. On the other hand, she used clever tricks to perfunctorily deal with Mr. Gu.

Since she swallowed this heavy bomb, she has been worried day and night. Recently, she has coughed up blood several times.

It seems that the creator is specifically making fun of her. The heavy bomb finally exploded.

It was on the evening of last Sunday that Gong and Gu unexpectedly met in her school. Undoubtedly, Mr. Gong was so angry that he fainted, while Mr. Gu used his cunning smile, forcing her into his trap. So she took this step—suicide, fortunately saved quickly, and is now well.

Starting yesterday, she has officially been living as a wife, while Mr. Gong, in extreme sadness, has gone to live his wandering life.

After she left, the colleagues all seemed to have lost something, and they did not see the arrival of spring, although at this time the peach blossoms are everywhere, showing off their tempting beauty.

Fairy Rainbow Clear Song

— Xinyun

For a year and a half, I often went to the Fairy Rainbow Society with my music friends Zhezun and Shouou to listen to the pure song without any worldly atmosphere. I actually became addicted. On average, I had to go once every three days. When I went, I always listened from the noisy gong and drum to the end of the performance, and I also had to bring a few music scores to carefully chew on. It was even more serious than attending class in school before. Therefore, I met several Kun opera performers worth admiring. Now, before they leave Shanghai to go elsewhere, I will write them out and introduce them to the public:

Zhu Chuanming - He is the pillar of the Fairy Rainbow Society, singing young female roles and supporting roles. He has the elegant name of Mei Lanfang of Kun opera. His specialty lies in the fact that his body, face, and hands all have drama, and the melody he sings is even more modulated, with rhythm and pace, making you feel unspeakable interest when you listen. And his daily private life is very proper and quiet, like a child of an old family.

Shen Chuankun - The painted face role is the most difficult role to sing. There are not many good painted face roles in Peking opera. In Kun opera, Mr. Shen really dominates. (However, he sings the martial painted face; Fairy Rainbow Society also has Mr. Shao Chuanyong, who specializes in civil painted face, and is also very good.) The Guan Gong opera he sings is especially outstanding, especially the "Single Pole Meeting". I dare say that there is no second person other than him. His sonorous voice is indeed no less than Mr. Jin Shaoshan.

Zhao Chuanjun - This one can be said to be the standard Tang Emperor. He sings "Hall of Eternal Life", and every part is good. Once, I went through heavy rain just to hear him sing "Listening to the Bells". After listening, I was extremely satisfied and couldn't wait to find Brother Muqin to introduce him to record records.

Ni Chuanyue - He sings male roles, supporting roles, or old male roles. Whether he wears a black beard or a white beard, his appearance is extremely pure. His voice is excellent. The "Ballad" and "Drafting the Edict" will make you listen to it and not know the taste of meat for three months.

Yao Chuanxiang - He sings supporting female roles and can perform many plays. No matter which role he plays, he will never disappoint people. Shouou said he was like Furong Cao in Peking opera, and that's indeed correct. He doesn't sing many main scenes, often pairing with people, but none of the old connoisseurs do not praise him. He can indeed be regarded as a very capable person.

In addition, Zhou Chuanying, Zhang Chuanfang, Shi Chuanzhen, and Shen Chuanzhi, Zhu Chuanqian, etc., each have their own special skills, which cannot be written out all at once; there is also the rising star Fang Chuanyun, who sings seriously and is willing to listen to others. Yun will definitely be an outstanding person in the future.

Varying Degrees of Seriousness!

Short Story

The Drunkard

— Juanlong

A few rays of dawn broke through the cracks in the walls and leaked in through the window holes, but the room was still dim. Hu Dahai, who had been drunk all night, was supposed to be awake at this time as usual. His mouth was dry and bitter, and his stomach was rumbling. He rolled out of bed, and habitually tossed the old black cloth quilt, which had been dyed with a layer of dirty blue flowers, towards the inside of the bed. He picked up the cup of cold tea left over from last night, which had seeped into a layer of ash, and sent it to his mouth—

"Damn it! If you don't return to your hometown, I won't drink this cold tea anymore!"

He opened his hazy, lost eyes and saw a "mirror box" next to the teacup that his wife used to dress up in the past, and he muttered again. But muttering was his old habit, and the death of his wife and children had no effect on squeezing out a tear.

He has forgotten when he last wore his clothes, and he doesn't know if he has changed them—perhaps he has no clothes to change, and he doesn't know how to wash them. Every night, after getting drunk, he sleeps in his clothes until dawn. The front of his clothes has been stained with wine stains, oil stains, and saliva, which has accumulated like a barber's stropping cloth. He has completely forgotten how many months he has not cut his hair and beard.

For the sake of wine, he squandered a small fortune. His brother also treated him like a dead person. He is a lonely person, but he did not feel that this was sad—his heart has been stiffened by the wine. Since his wife and children died, he loved wine even more. Half a kilogram, a few peanuts, he sat calmly on the street, drinking alone, like a living god. Once the wine reached a certain amount, his mouth would mutter incessantly like the water of the Yellow River. But what was he muttering? No one could hear it, and no one wanted to listen. When he was excited, he would curse loudly! Who was he cursing? Even he himself couldn't figure it out! He cursed whoever he thought of, and whoever heard it would give him a beating. But he wouldn't resist, but said:

—Old brother! You won't be wrong to hit me! You will always be good to me!

Go ahead and hit me!"

The person who hit him and the shop assistants who were lying on the counter laughed it off. When his brother saw this situation, he could only sigh—

"Alas! The ancestors have never done anything bad, but they gave birth to such a "loser", it's also "fate"!"

Sometimes, when Hu Dahai didn't have money to buy wine, he would vent his anger on his brother:

"Humph! You are relieved to inherit Afa's share of the property! You still have two sons earning money outside! You are relieved!…… You look down on me! Hey! You are just relying on your two sons! I am broke! I am finished!……"

His brother originally ignored him, but sometimes he really couldn't stand to hear it! He slapped him a few times! "You damned ghost, are you angry that my two sons are better than you? Are you angry that I got Afa's property? You can also have sons to inherit! Do you want to squander all the property of these three houses for you to drink?"

He touched his red face—

"Okay! You hit me! It's right for the older brother to hit the younger brother! I'm wrong! I'm wrong……

His footsteps were light and heavy, and his body seemed to be a paper shell. Even on a flat road, he would fall down. Sometimes his teeth fell out with blood, sometimes a piece of skin was scraped off his face, sometimes his face was stained with mud, sometimes…… But he didn't feel any pain or shame—

"Okay! You hit me! I……I deserve to die! You……good……." Then he let out a sinister laugh.

He stepped into the low and dilapidated house, which was dark and filled with a cloud of gray steam. The old and dilapidated furniture that had faded red paint was covered with a layer of ash. The room was very desolate, like an abandoned ancient temple.

But as soon as he lay down on the bed, he fell asleep.

Record of Lingering Fragrance

— Written by Princess Deling of Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

To embroider a pair, you have to re-stretch this square of tribute satin, so that the second shoe upper to be embroidered can be moved up, so that the person embroidering doesn't have to lower their head to accommodate it, which can save a little bit of eyesight. However, the four or five shoe uppers on each piece of tribute satin can never be embroidered with the same kind of flower. Often the first shoe upper is embroidered with plum blossoms, while the second is embroidered with peonies. Therefore, the person embroidering has no old articles to copy, and must cut out paper flowers again, and find another fresh flower that can be used as a specimen, re-determine the location, and choose the color. The experience gained from embroidering the first shoe upper is simply useless at all. The waste of energy is indescribable. No wonder I would shake my head when I first saw it!

When all the procedures are fully prepared—that is to say, the pattern on the shoe upper has been embroidered, the heel and the sole have been nailed together, and the shoe upper has been sewn to the sole to form a complete phoenix shoe—there is still a final procedure, which is the procedure of mounting ornaments such as jewelry. The Empress Dowager's phoenix shoes have all kinds of precious ornaments such as pearls, gemstones, jade, and jadeite. But what she loves most is pearls. She often said that pearls are the most suitable decoration for phoenix shoes. She likes pearls of all sizes. Therefore, almost none of her phoenix shoes are not studded with pearls. The smaller pearls are strung together with silk thread, strung like a lace, and then curved and bent and nailed to the shoe upper. Although the only thing that connects them is a very thin silk thread, which seems easy to break, I have lived in the palace for several years, but I have never seen them break, nor have I ever heard of anyone picking up a pearl that fell from the Empress Dowager's phoenix shoes. (299)

Commercial News

Finance

Holiday Affects Foreign and Local Bank Surges; Benchmark Gold Price Breaks 800 Yuan Mark; Once Reaching a New Low of 793 Yuan; A Sharp Drop of 9.8 Yuan Compared to Before the Holiday Closure

Due to the Spring Festival holiday closure, the gold market has been inactive for days. During this period, overseas silver markets have risen. Coupled with the closure of two major native banks in the city, the market was indirectly stimulated, resulting in a significant drop yesterday. Initially, due to the Spring Festival holiday, overseas silver markets in the UK and the US both rose. Dealers also claimed that after the market closed, transactions occurred above the listed price of 1875. The forward silver price in Montreux also increased, and exchange rates slightly decreased. London's raw gold rose by three pence, boosting confidence in the downstream market. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened, immediately retreating to 8067 yuan. With supply exceeding demand, buyers were hesitant, exacerbating the selling pressure, further breaking the 800 yuan mark. The central bank's listed prices were announced, with both the UK and the US rising, but the customs gold unit fell by eight li. The benchmark gold standard price dropped to 862 yuan and 7 jiao. The morning opening was even lower. Although some sought to cover their short positions after the opening, the rise was temporary due to traffic congestion. As soon as there was supply, selling pressure rose again, continuing the decline to a new low of 793 yuan. The foreign exchange market remained stable, and major players took advantage of the low prices to maintain their positions, gradually pushing the price back up to outside the 800 yuan mark. Sellers became active at the higher prices. The silver equalization tax was announced without any changes. After this, there was a slight dip, but banks maintained their positions at the low prices. Banks on the Bund Suddenly Increase Deposits by Over Six Million; Demand for Head Money Skyrockets to Forty-Three Cents; Over Eight and a Half Million in Long-Term Fourth-Bottom Transfers; No New Borrowing Seen as Over One Million Recalled

The market situation yesterday was such that, after rumors of collapses at Tong Tai and other banks, public sentiment gradually wavered. Deposits from various small banks and native banks were frantically withdrawn and deposited at banks on the Bund, amounting to over six million yuan. This caused temporary market chaos and tightened credit conditions. While the interbank lending rate remained at ten cents, the demand for "head money" (urgent short-term loans) soared, opening at forty cents and closing at forty-three cents, a more than tenfold increase compared to previous days. This was indeed a significant jump. In the interbank bill market, transfers totaled over 3.9 million yuan in the morning session, with over 400,000 yuan in new transactions. The afternoon session saw over 500,000 yuan in transactions. Transactions in the Small General Association amounted to over 800,000 yuan. Redemptions from foreign pawnshops totaled over 800,000 yuan, with new loans amounting to over 900,000 yuan. Recalls of currency transactions totaled over 700,000 yuan, with over 500,000 yuan issued. Furthermore, over 1.2 million yuan in secretly marked notes were issued, with over 600,000 yuan in remittances from various routes, incoming funds from other regions at 200,000 yuan and outgoing funds at 150,000 yuan. Xinfeng Trading House reported that yesterday (April 22) the New York stock market trended upwards. Utilities and Industrials both reached new highs for the year. Over a Thousand Bales of Yarn Awaiting Delivery

The yarn market has shown signs of stability after the major drop the previous day. New sellers are relatively scarce. This Month's Cotton Futures Fluctuations: Prior Market Sell-Off Followed by Later Market Replenishment; Distant Futures Rise in the Morning but Fall in the Afternoon

The cotton market this month is gradually showing a weak state. According to market reports, the cotton that has passed inspection by the cotton inspection office has reached about 9,000 bales. As a result, many speculators, seeing sufficient delivery, are settling their excess positions, and the market is becoming slack. However, some industry players are inclined to go long. It is estimated that, overall, the price ratio between cotton and yarn suggests that cotton prices are high.

At the opening of the spot cotton market, the market condition was sluggish, showing a state of standstill. This was because U.S. cotton fell by four to six points, and Indian cotton rose sharply by five rupees. However, the spot price fell sharply, breaking through the 800 yuan mark, reaching a new low, and causing a weary and dispirited sentiment. However, major players are firmly absorbing the volume and not letting go. It is said that there will be 10,000 bales for delivery this month, and scattered long positions are being settled, making the market particularly weak, down 25 cents from the previous day's close. Grains: Relationship Between Wheat Futures and the Exchange Rate—Large Arrivals of Spot Wheat, Market Slightly Smaller—

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was generally flat and weak. The quoted price for foreign wheat was only slightly better by about four points. At the opening, due to the sharp fall in the gold market, although sellers did not dump heavily, everyone was watching and waiting. As a result, the market showed a weak and lifeless atmosphere. Domestic new wheat will soon enter the market, making it impossible to continue ordering foreign wheat. However, a prolonged extension of foreign exchange is tantamount to a counter-proof that continuous purchases are possible. Perhaps this is why buyers could not be attracted. As a result, the current month was down 0.2 cents, July was down 0.2 cents, August was down 0.4 cents, and September was down 0.2 cents. In the spot wheat market, due to abundant arrivals and mills not being greedy, prices for each grade fell by 0.2-0.3 cents. The opening price for Bengbu wheat was 3.97 yuan, followed by 3.95 yuan; Yingzhou wheat was 3.99 yuan; Luohe wheat was 3.94 yuan, followed by 3.92 yuan; Xinpu wheat was 3.87 yuan, followed by 3.85 yuan; Haizhou wheat was 3.91 yuan; Jiangbei wheat was 3.90 yuan; Pingxi wheat was 3.92 yuan; Hankou wheat was 3.79 yuan, followed by 3.75 yuan. A total of 6,000 bags were handled by Fuxin. There is very little high-grade deliverable wheat in Chicago; most of the hedges have already been moved. The spot wheat situation is firm. The major early-harvest areas still have no rain. It is expected that the supply will decrease by 2.162 million bushels this week.

Flour Turns Weak After Remaining Steady

Yesterday, the flour market was first steady and then fell. The quoted price for foreign wheat from Chicago and Canada was slightly better by about 0.4 cents. After the opening, as financial rumors had subsided, but the exchange rate rose sharply and gold prices fell sharply, the current month's opening price was low at 0.3 cents, a drop of 0.6 cents from the previous week's high, although spot prices were still rising. This was because actual sales were slightly stagnant due to turnover issues. Distant futures were stable as factories were not selling. The current month rebounded by 0.1 cents due to short-covering. However, at the afternoon opening, the opening prices for all months were initially stable, but then long positions were sold off, and factories also slightly sold, causing all near and distant months to show a weak and declining trend. Observing this situation, if the weather is good and actual sales are stagnant due to financial reasons, the market may be weaker. As a result, the current month fell by 0.75 cents, May fell by 0.1 cent, June fell by 0.75 cents, July fell by 1.25 cents, August fell by 1.75 cents, and September fell by 1.75 cents.

Rice Prices Mostly See Small Declines—Undoubtedly Related to Tight Credit—

The market for foreign Indica rice initially had a trend of continuing to rise, but was affected by changes in the financial world. Importers of foreign Indica rice mostly took a wait-and-see attitude, and the rising trend of foreign Indica rice was immediately thwarted. Yesterday, Japan Street and the Yangtze River regions stopped trading, while inland purchases continued to be active, handling over 20,000 bags of rice and over 1,000 bags of foreign Indica rice. Prices were similar to the previous market, and spot prices remained firm.

Yesterday, only the 13th and 14th batches of river rice arrived at various Shanghai South Bank suppliers (totaling nearly 3,000 stones). Sales were also normal, and the situation was quiet. Later, over 500 bags from Qingdao and Yantai suppliers arrived, which tightened the market and brought stability. The supply of regular Shanghai, Suzhou, Tongxiang, Nangang, and other japonica rice varieties, as well as Qingjiao, Songjiang, Xishi, and Lianxi thin rice varieties, was scarce, and prices were unchanged. The prices of Yinyuan and Yangjian rice varieties also did not fluctuate. In the Shanghai North rice market yesterday, the 22nd and 23rd batches of river rice arrived in Shanghai. Sales were slow, and transactions were sluggish. Market prices for white japonica rice were down about 0.1 yuan, and prices for high-quality thin rice were down nearly 0.1 yuan. Prices for medium and low-quality thin rice and early rice were slightly down. The price of Bianyuan rice was down 0.2 yuan. Other varieties also showed a weak trend.

Inland Sales of Red Sorghum and Corn Continue to Be Strong—Opening Prices All Up 0.05-0.07 Yuan

The market for red sorghum and corn is gradually becoming strong. Due to continuous inland sales, the market saw a sudden increase in buying interest yesterday, so sellers were hoarding, and prices rose. Overall, the market sold 600 bags of Guide red sorghum, four truckloads of Bengbu red sorghum, and 240 bags of Tianjin corn, all of which were purchased for inland sales. Corn prices were up 0.05 yuan, and red sorghum prices were up 0.06-0.07 yuan compared to the previous market. The bean market is still fluctuating. Although factories have demand, they seem to be losing steam. Inland trade in this area is also difficult to develop due to financial depletion and a somewhat discouraged sentiment, making it difficult for selling prices to rise. Overall, the market sold 1,000 bags of Guide beans, one truckload of Feihe beans, 200 bags of Yingzhou beans, one truckload of Quanhe beans, 200 bags of Hankou Zha beans, 147 bags of Gou beans, 300 bags of Chi beans, and 100 bags of Chongming sandy yellow beans. Truckloads of beans were still purchased by factories. Prices were similar to before. The futures price of beans was slightly down by 0.03 yuan in the current month but still up by 0.02 yuan in May. The market had no unique characteristics.

Sugar Market: Sugar Transactions Are Also Quite Scarce

The sugar market is seeing loose customs gold and extremely tight credit, resulting in scarce transactions and a softening trend. The association set the market price for 24 groups of granulated white sugar at 17.40 yuan, and the re-export price was down 0.05 yuan to 5.70 yuan, but no transactions were made. The quoted price for Zhenyu No. 1 refined white sugar from local factories was 16.80 yuan. Only a few dozen bags of Hainan red sugar were offered by the Chaozhou group at a price of 10.06 yuan, unchanged from before. A hundred or so pieces of large-bag tribute ice sugar arrived from the Taiyuan freighter for the Jian group yesterday. Samples will be available today, and the market outlook is stable.

Silk and Tea: News of Keemun New Tea

Keemun black tea has become increasingly popular recently. The number of tea production workshops has increased to 240. Among them, 30 production and sales cooperatives funded by the Chinese Farmers Bank have completed their general vote and unanimously passed the confidence motion, entrusting all sales to Qianji Tea Shop in Shanghai. Tea farmers also started picking on the 20th. Due to the weather being neither cold nor warm, with sunny days and rainy nights, the quality of the tea is much better than in previous years, with a production volume of around 50,000 boxes.

Zhenmei Green Tea Sees New Low Price Again

There has been renewed interest in European sales of Luzhuang chouxin Zhenmei green tea recently. Yesterday, Zhongxinchang, Shengchang, and Shengchang tea shops, together with Tongfu, Hua Tea, and other firms, reached an agreement on Wuyuan high-grade goods, totaling over 120 boxes. The market price opened at 78 yuan. This price is 60% lower than the opening price last year, the lowest price in recent years.

Metals: Union Steel Inventory Is Thin

The new bottom inventory of 200-pound Union Steel is very thin, and the outlets are actively collecting and handling by guest gangs and factories. The market situation is very active, and the market conditions for standard quality are extremely good. The estimated price for old steel mill goods is 29.50 yuan, and the estimated price for new steel mill goods is 28.75 yuan. A type of chicken goods can also be opened up to 27.50 yuan. It is reported that a total of two or three hundred boxes were opened in the past two days, and the market sentiment is extremely good. The market prospects for tomorrow are very solid.

Free Talk

The Life and Works of D.H. Lawrence

— Ren Baitao

D.H. Lawrence was born on September 11, 1885, in Nottinghamshire. His father was a coal miner. Lawrence was the fourth among his siblings. At the age of thirteen, he won a scholarship to Nottingham High School. At the age of sixteen, he left school and worked in a surgical instrument manufacturing factory. But at the age of eighteen, he entered Nottingham University to obtain a teacher's certificate. At this university, he met the famous linguist Professor E. Weekly and began writing his debut work, "The White Peacock." His mother suffered from cancer and died in 1910. He wanted his mother to see "The White Peacock" before she died, so he specially printed a copy, but his mother never saw it. After studying at Nottingham University for two years, he obtained a teacher's certificate and took a teaching position at the David Road School in Croydon, near London. During this teaching period, he wrote many essays, short stories, and poems. It was not his mother but his lover—the girl who was "Miriam" in "Son and Lovers"—who encouraged him to write. She herself sent five of his poems to the magazine "English Review," which was in 1909. After being published by F.M. Huefier, the editor of this magazine, Lawrence officially entered the British literary scene. This was the person who introduced "The White Peacock" to be published by Hanniel Society (1911). During this time, he also published several essays and essays in Heffa's magazine. After two years, he resigned from his teaching position and devoted himself to writing. Not long after leaving the school in Croydon, he was hired as a lecturer by a German university, but he declined. But soon he went to Germany and served in Bavaria for six months, then went to Lake Garda in Italy. During this time, his second novel, "The Trespasser," was published (1912).

In February 1913, his first collection of poems, "Love Poems and Others," was published. Two months later, his masterpiece "Sons and Lovers" was also published. At this time, he lived in the capital of Bavaria. He returned to England in June and stayed temporarily on the coast of Kent. He went to Bavaria again in August. He went to Italy in September. In the Gulf of Spezia, he lived there until June of the following year.

In July 1914, he returned to England and married Frieda, the daughter of a German baron von Richthofen. But Frida was originally the daughter of Professor Weekly, his old teacher during his university days, eight years older than him, and had already had three children. Details of this romance are written in "The Savage Pilgrimage," a memoir of Lawrence by his female disciple C. Carswell. Also in this year, his first collection of short stories, "The Prussian Officer," was published. In December, the two lived in Casersham, Buckinghamshire, northwest of London. In January of the following year, they moved to Pulborough in Sussex on the south coast.

In August 1915, he moved to the outskirts of London. In September, "The Rainbow" was published. This novel was banned from distribution in name because it harmed public morals, but in fact, it contained anti-war elements, which offended the authorities' taboos. The ban on the sale of "The Rainbow" was a severe blow to Lawrence. Regarding this incident, only M. Sinclair and A. Bennelt did some sympathetic advocacy in the literary world, and no one else helped him. The persecution he suffered during the war was more than this: just because his wife was German, he lived on the coast of Cornwall and was suspected by the local authorities of colluding with the enemy, who searched his home. How he suffered during the war can be understood by reading the chapter "The Nightmare" in "Kangaroo." Poverty and other oppressions, repeated distribution bans, and illness—his life was a history of bitter struggle.

His Cornwall period was from December 1915 to October 1917. During this period, he published the essays "Twilight in Italy" and the poetry collection "Amores." From October 1917 to January of the following year, he lived in London, then moved to Newbruy in Burke County, and in May came to Middleton in Derby County. In November 1919, after the end of the war, he crossed to Italy: he lived in Florence until December, then went to the island of Capri; in March of the following year, he moved to Taormina on the east coast of Sicily. In April 1921, he left this place and entered Germany via Italy, residing in Baden. During this time, his fourth novel, "Women in Love," was published by Seka Society in London (1921); but this novel had already been published in a limited edition by pre-order in New York (1920). The couple then returned from Baden to Sicily. That winter, Lawrence traveled to Sardinia in the Mediterranean Sea; his harvest was the publication of "Sea and Sardinia" (New York 1921; London 1923).

In 1922, Lawrence and his wife went to India and stayed in Ceylon for two months. Then he crossed to Australia, for about three months. The publication of "Aaron's Rod" was at that time. In August 1922, the couple left Australia, and via New York and the South Pacific Islands, arrived in San Francisco in September. From there, he went to Taos, New Mexico; then to Mexico.

In the autumn of 1923, Lawrence roamed Quan Guan and returned to Mexico. In August 1923, his wife returned to England, and he returned in November. After returning to China, he lived there until the end of January of the following year, and the two went to Baden and Paris again, and then returned to London; but in March, they took a ship to the United States again: this time, they sailed directly to New Mexico. He lived in New Mexico until October 1924, and then went to Oaxaca in southern Mexico. There he collected most of the material for "Mornings in Mexico" and completed "The Plumed Serpent" (1926); the short stories later collected in "The Woman Who Rode Away" were also written at that time.

Lawrence returned to England in October 1925; but immediately went to Frida's mother's home in Baden; then to Spotorno, where he lived until March 1926. During this time, "The Plumed Serpent" was published.

The couple moved from Spotorno to Florence and rented a villa outside the city. Here, Lawrence began to write his last novel, "Lady Chatterley's Lover." This novel was rewritten three times, and the first edition was a signed limited private edition printed by G. Orioli in Florence (1928). Apart from short trips to Germany, England, and Switzerland, the couple lived in the villa in Florence until May 1928.

From March to November 1928, his whereabouts were Switzerland, Germany, and southern France, and finally settled in Bandol, where he lived until 1929.

They then traveled to Paris and Florence. In April 1929, they lived in the Balearic Islands near the Mediterranean Sea in Spain for more than a month. It was during this time that he decided to open a painting exhibition in London. But this exhibition was interfered with by the London authorities and failed to open. Later, those works were moved to Vence in southern France. In the summer of the same year, he traveled to Germany; his collection of poems "Pansies" was published during this time.

In February 1930, he moved to the mountains of Vence. Died of illness on March 2. He suffered from bronchitis and wheezing, and was confined to a room on rainy days. His British friends received a notice that he was ill and thought it was nothing serious, but he unexpectedly died a few days later. Therefore, there were only forty or so people who attended the funeral. Before his grave, only the "Phoenix"—which he had long chosen as his own pattern—made of small stones collected by a farmer who loved him, stood there like something symbolizing.

Curiosities Gathered

— Wo Pu

"Record of the West Tower"

Li Diaoyuan's "Yucun Quhua" Volume II has the following:

"The most taboo in composing music is to go beyond reason and emotion; Wang Shungeng's 'Record of the West Tower', when matchmaking fails, he lets out an old (note: should be 胥) Gong, kills an innocent concubine, and steals someone's concubine as a friend's wife. The structure has reached this point, which can be said to be falling into a sea of misery. Shungeng, a native of Gaoyou."

The next item says:

"West Tower is good at adjusting rhythms. The white words in the sixth scene "Private Contract" say: "I have seen the glorious mansion of Jin Fan, and I praise his great name day and night." This is Shungeng's self-satisfaction. Therefore, it is said: "To children, the ancient melodies of Yangchun, few harmonize."

Li's claims that Wang Shungeng of Gaoyou wrote the "Record of the West Tower." These two records make a double mistake. Li did not even know who Yuan Ziling was at the time, which is strange—the reason why he "entangled" Wang Shungeng was probably because of the confusion caused by the loose song collection "West Tower Music House". The differences between loose songs and dramas were originally very confused and indistinguishable. Probably, Li happened to not know who the author of the "Record of the West Tower" was, so he confusedly linked it with Wang Shungeng. But at the end of the Ming Dynasty, there were indeed two people named West Tower; one was Wang Pan, named Hongjian, from Gaoyou. One was Wang Tian, named Shungeng, from Jinan. Both Wangs were Sanqu writers with great reputation. People who talked about music in the Ming Dynasty could not distinguish them very clearly, and they often referred to them interchangeably. The existing "West Tower Music House" was written by Wang Hongjian. (See Ren Erbei's "Anthology of Loose Songs" and "Quxie") The Gaoyou Wang Shungeng mentioned by Li has also made mistakes in his place of origin and writings. This does not seem to be able to be simply blamed on him.

In the past, books discussing music, apart from "Yucun Quhua", also included Liang Tingnan's "Teng Hua Ting Quhua", Yang Enshou's "Ciyu Conghua", all of which often made this kind of mistake of "talking according to conjecture". If we want to base their records as "essentials", especially for more obscure materials, we probably cannot but pay special attention to selection, identification and review.

Dance Marathon (3)

— (By American L.T. Farrell, Translated by Yi Xian)

Then, hard times came to America. Tax lost his job in winter, and his savings were gone again. He was hired by a candy store, working twelve hours a day, ten dollars a week, but after ten months, he lost that job too. He entered a large restaurant, doing dishwashing work, seven dollars a week, and later his wages were reduced to five dollars. Every night, with stiff hands and aching back, he walked home tiredly. He had no money to go to dance halls anymore. Later, he lost even this dishwashing job.

He walked the streets, looking for other work, and all he heard was the same story—hard times. He ate very sparingly, lived in a single, cold room with many rats, and wished he could return to his hometown in the Greek mountains. He went out every day looking for work. Sometimes he found short-term jobs, getting by for a few days or weeks, then struggling to find work again. One day, he saw an advertisement with large letters—Dance Marathon. After some investigation, he learned that it was a competition where participants had to dance as hard as they could, and whoever danced the longest would be the winner, with a prize of five hundred dollars. Maybe he would win the championship in this competition. Then, he could get a position in the movie industry and become the dream lover of American girls. Otherwise, he could perform at a cabaret or sign a dance contract with some tavern. Moreover, during the competition, he would be taken care of, having food to eat and not having to pay rent. He was strong and knew how to dance. He was used to standing on his feet all day long in restaurants, candy stores, and taverns. This was truly his chance to make a fortune. He wouldn't have to run around listening to people say they weren't hiring because of the hard times. This was much better than saving up money to open a candy store himself, like those Greek-Americans who had employed him, gradually becoming rich. If he won this competition and became famous, he could return to Athens with suitcases full of clothes and foreign money, perhaps even with a rich American wife with milk-like skin.

Tax joined the "Dance Marathon." He was given a number to wear on his back and assigned a dance partner named Mary Green, a beautiful blue-eyed girl who was exactly the type he had always dreamed of marrying. At first, when this girl met him, she couldn't help but feel a shock and show a disgusted expression on her face. However, she quickly realized that he was a strong, broad-shouldered man, and she smiled charmingly, offering him a soft hand and saying sweetly that she knew they would definitely win the championship.

An Evening Call

— Shi Ye

Speaking of this story, it has been a long time ago, but even now, I often think about it and cannot forget...

It was an autumn evening two years ago. I brought the news of my late wife's death to a relative named Yao, to inform them that my wife, who had been ill for a year and a half, had finally passed away, leaving behind only a four-year-old child and myself.

The Yao family lived in a spacious single-family house. Because there were many people, they even borrowed the adjacent downstairs guest room, with a door connecting them. When I entered, the guest room was silent. Only a doctor sat at a mahogany table, writing a prescription with a brush, making rustling sounds. Yao's father, over sixty years old, with white hair and beard, sat opposite the doctor, his face furrowed; Yao's mother, of the same age, had become somewhat slow-witted after a fire scare, her head lowered, sitting blankly in a corner. The gloomy autumn twilight was gradually enveloping the guest room, which was filled with a sense of sorrow and desolation.

Because I hadn't visited for a long time, the two elders stood up to welcome me, showing a little smile on their faces. They immediately noticed the black gauze on my arm and asked in surprise who had passed away. I replied that it was my wife.

"Oh, what a pity. What illness was it?" the two elders asked in unison.

"Lung disease. It started after January 28th."

"When did she pass away?"

"A week ago."

The two elders listened silently. On their faces, there was a look of sympathy and regret, but also of pain. At that moment, the doctor had finished writing the prescription, and as he stood up, he said, "Try taking two doses of this."

"Is it Xiujie who is sick again?" I asked.

"Yes, her illness flares up every now and then. This time it's quite severe. We've already consulted three or four doctors," Yao's mother replied sadly.

From the downstairs guest room next door, which served as a bedroom, came two or three soft coughs. The guest room where I was sitting became as quiet as if water had been poured on it. The two elders' eyes became moist, and the doctor stared at the black gauze on my arm.

Finally, the doctor left, leaving only the two elderly people and myself, who had lost his wife. The sky grew darker.

I had wanted to go to the next room to check on Xiujie's condition, but I thought that Xiujie's illness was also lung disease, and it was said that there was some karmic connection with my late wife according to superstition, so I didn't get up after all. A faint sadness welled up in my heart, and I looked at the two elders, thinking of that unbelievable karmic connection.

It turned out that five years before, on the day I married my late wife, Xiujie had helped along with her other sisters. Xiujie was the one who dressed the bride. However, because of a small quarrel during the wedding, my late wife, who had a fiery temper, got angry while being dressed and knocked into Xiujie with her hand, and the wooden comb also fell to the ground. According to superstition, this was unlucky for the person helping with the bride's attire. Afterwards, Xiujie, who was physically weak, became ill. According to Yao's mother privately, the initial cause was that the bride had knocked her with her hand. Other older people also said the same. From then on, I felt a faint sense of guilt and fear of unspoken blame, and I rarely went to their house.

Now, unexpectedly, Xiujie had been ill for several years, and my late wife, who had been healthy, had also contracted lung disease and passed away first. Thinking of this, I felt an indescribable grief.

I woke up from my thoughts and looked up to see a photo of Xiujie hanging on the wall, taken after she became ill. Her delicate face had a kind of lingering sorrow. Her eyes were gentle but contained a hint of sadness. From the next room, I heard the light, clear sound of coughing again.

That evening, the two elders earnestly urged me to stay for dinner, but I felt as if I were burdened with a heavy crime and didn't dare to sit for long. I excused myself, saying I had other business, and hurriedly left, only leaving a word of regards for Xiujie, leaving the two elders alone in the lonely autumn evening, taking care of their young daughter, because on that day, her sisters-in-law were not at home.

This young woman, who was still unmarried, also passed away last spring. On the way to the funeral, I silently prayed for the reconciliation and peace of the two deceased.

"You two are both people I loved and respected, and unfortunately, you both died young. If dying young is fortunate, then you have been fortunate.

"You two, please reconcile in another world, because death is reconciliation."

Pastoral in the Mountains (3)

— Ai Wu

When he realized that they would be traveling together tomorrow and the day after, he softened his expression and made a show of carefully listening to what the other party was saying. However, he wouldn't lower himself too much, always looking for opportunities to hint vaguely about how he had once done big business.

"Three strings and two hundred cash? Hah, my shop used to pay only two strings and four hundred cash! This..."

Or, when talking about how smuggling opium could make a lot of money, he would shake his head and say:

"We don't do that kind of business... That's simply harming people! To be honest, we look down on money earned that way. Trading foreign cloth and yarn is the right way to go, I'm telling you, brother."

Because, hearing this kind of thing, Lao Xu, who did a little bit of small business, couldn't help but feel respect, and when the shop owner brought the food, he treated him with the face of a peddler treating a good customer, squinting his eyes surrounded by wrinkles and politely inviting him:

"Boss Qin, please take a seat! Please take a seat!"

"Don't be so polite!"

Even though he said that, Boss Qin didn't give way to the other party and went ahead and sat down. Lao Chen, who was in the business of selling smuggled cigarettes, had long felt extremely unhappy, and now he could only bury his head in his food. When Boss Qin left, Lao Chen knocked his chopsticks on his bowl and said to Lao Xu:

"Damn it, is selling foreign goods more noble? That's ridiculous!... In the end, in one sentence, they are slaves of foreigners!"

But the next morning, the man called Boss Qin actually argued with the shop owner over not wanting to exchange a broken copper coin to pay for the shop, and Lao Chen also canceled his opinion that he was some kind of boss, lightly leaning his elbow on Lao Xu and whispering:

"Look, would someone who has been a big boss be like this? You actually believed him!"

So, on the road, everyone was encouraging Lao Xu to oppose Boss Qin.

After someone on a trip has expressed his unhappiness, if he can sing a little, he will sing whatever comes to mind. Now, Lao Chen was exactly in this situation, so he began to sing mountain songs, starting with his own male voice, with a teasing tone.

"Three elder sisters-in-law cross the west river,

The one in the middle is my wife!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Banning Polygamy and Trafficking of Women and Children

— Qiong Sheng

A dispatch from Eastman Port on the 21st, carrying a message about the "International Women's Movement," stated: "The International Women's Rights Conference recently held here passed a resolution stipulating that there should be no distinction between East and West in prohibiting the trafficking of white women and banning polygamy, and that there should be no discrimination in the treatment of women based on their nationality or religion." In many parts of our country, the trafficking of women is not only widespread but also reduced in price to two or three dollars or valued by age (one dollar per year). At the same time, after the abolition of the "concubine system," the "family relationship" of "cohabitation" between men and women is very prevalent. This resolution is worth discussing.

I am not a woman, so I cannot experience what it is like to be reduced to "commodities" and fall into the life of a "concubine." However, history and reality have recorded for me that some are called "cattle and horses," and others are called "toys." Generally speaking, they are not treated as "people." Creatures with all five senses and round heads and square feet cannot receive the same treatment as their male counterparts. This is indeed a "miracle" of "human society." This "miracle" exists among birds, beasts, snakes, and insects and seems worthy of special attention from our biologists. However, it occurs among us, who have reached the twentieth century and even call ourselves "civilized," and is regarded as a matter of course, ignored by familiar eyes. It's truly "God knows!"

This "God knows" matter, if it were practiced in the era of "the husband being the guide of the wife," it would be fine. However, now we constantly talk about "respecting women's rights" and "gender equality," which makes it difficult for us to justify ourselves. The gentlemen of the International Women's Rights Conference have raised their voices to prohibit and eliminate this. Without a doubt, I raise both hands to express my support. However, I doubt whether this "resolution" alone can successfully eliminate the phenomenon of trafficking women and the bad habit of polygamy.

The existence of social inequality, where some people eat others and some people plunder others, leads to the occurrence of trafficking women. Only in such an environment will some people be willing to sell women, and only some people will have the right and possibility to buy women. Brokers of trafficking women only play a side effect in the process and are "produced by market needs." However, the gentlemen of the women's rights movement, setting aside the root of the problem, seize the accomplices as the main culprits and try to prohibit them. I have not seen that this will be effective.

Noble People

— Jing Fu

People who pass through Chen Jia Zhuang often sigh with admiration: "Oh, that's the house of Master Chen the Second!" After many years of wind and rain, this elegant and grand building is still so majestic and strong. Master Chen the Second is the first wealthy man in Chen Jia Zhuang, a truly noble person! Everyone still remembers the former prestige of the noble Master Chen the Second.

However, since Master Chen the Second returned to his hometown for the fifth time, things have changed.

Now, in front of Master Chen the Second's mansion, which still makes people yearn for it at first glance, many children are running around every day, often encountering a terrifying person.

Page 18

The children like to tease him and even play pranks on him. This terrifying person is the formerly intimidating and noble Master Chen the Second. In the past, the children were so amazed, admired, and fearful of him. He brought back a lot of money from Southeast Asia and became a truly noble person. However, his last glorious return home also brought leprosy. Leprosy, what a terrifying term!

Master Chen the Second's noble sons, daughters-in-law, and wives are not in this mansion accompanying him. They are all in Southeast Asia guarding the mutually rich property. Only two servants cover their noses and snicker when they see him, considering it service to him. The deep and tall mansion is too empty. Master Chen the Second often pulls on his cane, swaying his swollen body and festering face, appearing in front of the mansion. Although the children are annoying, they are better than lying dead in the house, more lively and energetic.

As soon as the swollen body appears at the door, the children cover their noses, point at him, and shout: "Oh, oh, leper... leper..." The children are afraid of this leper whose whole body is rotting but also like to approach him to joke and have fun. If he tries to sway back inside, they hurry up and block the door: "Leper, leper, don't go..." They giggle and clap, and some even throw twigs and pebbles at him, clapping their hands and shouting for joy.

On his hands, feet, and face, there are sores, yellow pus, slightly red wounds, and poisonous juices about to drip. Flies buzz around, constantly bothering Master Chen the Second. Master Chen the Second can only twist his flesh, showing his pain. Passersby often point and say: What a terrifying beggar! No one thinks that this is the once authoritative and noble person!

Yes! Master Chen the Second is a wealthy man from Southeast Asia. However, his meanness and stinginess are also well known. Many people who have suffered from him never expected this to be his end. Wealthy people love their money, but they also love all kinds of entertainment. Master Chen the Second is completely dissolute, but even more stingy with his money. So, he strongly disapproves of those who go to brothels and prostitutes. That's really foolish! Master Chen the Second came up with a method. He bought female servants, who could provide the same service as prostitutes every night and also work for him. This was the most cost-effective. As a result, Master Chen the Second contracted incurable leprosy from this "double-duty" female servant because of his greed for small advantages. Lepers are not tolerated by people and are expelled by foreigners. Finally, he lives alone in the noble mansion in loneliness. When he returned, everyone exclaimed: "How did Master Chen the Second become like this... Such a noble person!" But afterwards, people would mock the terrifying Master Chen to his face: "Miserliness leads to ruin, oh, you are very noble... but now...? So stingy..." At the same time, they would spit and walk away laughing.

"This is the most noble rich man! This is a despicable leper..."

Before and After Returning Home

— Chong Lin

(3)

As the ship entered Wusong Port, we began to see the fields, vegetation, and tiled roofs of China. I was very surprised. The impressions of the fields, vegetation, and tiled roofs of Europe were still clear in my mind. Suddenly, I felt that the scenery of China was so weak, withered, and small. Even the hairless deserts of Africa were more vibrant and energetic.

The sky was drizzling, with three flakes of snow, gloomy, just like the weather when we left Lyon. The ship was supposed to dock at ten in the morning, but there were big storms on the voyage from Hong Kong to Shanghai, delaying the arrival time. The sky gradually darkened. In the sea breeze with snow, we stood shivering, standing, standing from two in the afternoon, it was already past five in the afternoon, waiting for Shanghai to come closer to our eyes.

A few years ago, I left Shanghai with heavy wounds and humiliation. A few years ago, I also left Shanghai with the good intentions and high hopes of friends. How would I see it again? As I stepped on the shore of Shanghai, I understood: I was finally misunderstood, and a hidden malice was probing for opportunities to prepare to slander me again.

After a period of chaos, squeezing, and waiting at customs, we parted from our companion Mr. Wang and saw our relatives and friends. We had seen them long ago when the ship docked. An unspeakable joy made us intoxicated with tears. However, these joyful tears immediately turned into sad tears for me. I realized at this time that I was already an orphan who had lost his loving mother, a truly pitiful person.

Walking on the streets of Shanghai, the first things I found annoying and unaccustomed to, like in Hong Kong, were the advertisements, followed by the fashionable Shanghai women. Most of them had permed hair, which was scattered and fluffy like the head of a Western doll that had not been styled. Their clothing already knew how to make the waist thin and show the hips, but they still didn't know how to lift the chest. One lady said to me:

"The book 'Little Women' is very popular. We all love to read it. It can be said to be the best book in recent years."

This is a confession of a new woman. What do the ladies, misses, and gentlemen engaged in women's movement think?

In Shanghai, I felt that life was not at all like it was in Europe, full of work and other things. In Shanghai, days seemed to pass especially quickly. One afternoon, you could only see one friend, and you didn't sit for long in that friend's house. Later, I accidentally stood by the window of the hostel's service counter and discovered the reason for this. Walking on the streets of Shanghai, I felt very uncomfortable. It was as if there were walls blocking me in front and behind. These walls built for pedestrians are indeed a characteristic of Shanghai's Chinese commercial port. Among them, there are few people who are seriously doing things, and most are loitering on the road, stepping ants to death. They look around, talking and cursing. It is impossible to quickly reach your destination if you have urgent business. Your time is spent on these things. For example, to visit a friend, the road originally only takes half an hour, but you are blocked by these people, so it takes an hour. Another characteristic of Shanghai is the noise of people. Like in European cities, at the subway entrances when workers, shop assistants, and clerks go to work, the crowds are so dense that you only see a wave-like motion, but it is quiet and not as noisy as a small street in Shanghai.

(4)

I have also returned to this hometown that I left in my childhood. Everything is fresh to me, as if I am seeing it for the first time. Most of the surrounding neighbors and relatives, old ones, have died, and I don't know the young ones. It is indeed a bit like "children meet but do not recognize each other, asking with a smile where the guest has come from." In our room with square brick floors, from the glass window in the sitting room, we can see a narrow river. The other bank of the river is the so-called Hebei. The thatched huts of the Hebei people are still vaguely like ancient paintings. Several rice stacks are piled in the yard in front of our house. Outside the bamboo fence, at this time, the entire field is full of tender cabbage hearts, newly sprouted broad bean seedlings, and green dogwood grass.

Returning home, I felt that the most special and fresh things were the popularity of rubber overshoes and cigarettes. On rainy days, when walking on the muddy road to the town, the farmers with bamboo skirts all wore rubber overshoes. Even the ladies and young mistresses who chanted scriptures, ate vegetarian food, and spun thread to weave their own cloth – who did not smoke when I left the country before – now all have a cigarette in their mouths, taking a puff and exhaling a long breath, as if they couldn't wait to suck the ashes into their stomachs. One young mistress told me about the goodness of Japanese goods:

"It's really not easy to get people to use domestic products. Like spun silk is expensive and not good-looking. Japanese silk materials are cheap and good-looking."

Eight out of ten middle-aged and elderly men in the villages are opium smokers. Opium ghosts, this is another special product of our rice-producing hometown. Not long after I got home, because it was a season for advocating opium abstinence, everyone who smoked opium was discussing everything about opium abstinence.

They all admitted that opium addiction was more painful than having a fever. Several of them had already quit and relapsed.

"It's really too easy to relapse after quitting!" one said.

"Forced opium abstinence is not as good as banning opium altogether!" another said.

The shadows of the entire of China are reflected on the faces of these gaunt opium addicts.

Hong Ci Nunnery

— Yong Hui

The sound of the Buddha's name from Songshan Temple drifted from the dense forest opposite; the sound was aged and melancholic—a moaning from the heart of life!

The sound of the wooden fish from Hong Ci Nunnery echoed in harmony with the chanting. In the ancient nunnery, the lime on the walls was peeling off; the two small doors seemed to be worm-eaten: a piece of paint had fallen off on the east side, and there was a hole on the west…

The sound of the chime followed the sound of the wooden fish, seeping out of the moldy Buddhist hall along with wisps of incense smoke: the old nun's chanting sounded rusty, so weak and intermittent. Besides the old nun's voice, there was also a young nun chanting shrilly in harmony.

By the time the chanting was finished, it was already dusk.

"Alas! Is this compassion? Is this the compassion of a renunciate? It's truly living a life of suffering!" she sighed to herself while preparing the vegetarian meal: "Master is almost in the grave! And me? I'm only eighteen! If I go on like this, when will being a nun ever end…"

"Master tells me about the wonders of the Western Paradise, but in reality, if one suffers while alive, who cares about the benefits after death…"

In the gray-black hours before dawn, the young nun habitually got out of bed; she unconsciously and habitually draped a robe covered in dust over her body, not daring to linger in bed for even a moment, lest she violate the old nun's strict orders.

The light of the eternal lamp and the sound of the chime stirred her memories: it was as if she saw her distant hometown, shrouded in clouds and mist for over a year, and her parents, wandering and displaced; although her hometown had been destroyed by years of war and drought! And her parents' whereabouts were unknown due to the turmoil: this only made her yearn more for the beautiful dreams of the past! Recalling the finery she once possessed before becoming a nun.

Although she had been in the nunnery for more than a year, her youthful beauty had not been buried by the worn robe and the desolate years.

When a flame of hope burned within her heart: she could no longer restrain herself! The stern Arhat could not suppress the young person's desire for life, and the iron chains of rigid ethical doctrines could not lock up the vibrant young heart! She could not let her tears spin endlessly with the Buddhist beads in her hands, nor could she let her youth fade away with the lonely time! On a snowy midnight, she mustered her courage, abandoned the harsh old nun, and embarked on the boundless journey of life, beginning to pursue her new life.

Night Anchorage at West Market

— Tian Qi

In the fading twilight, the boat slowly pulled into the South Embankment of West Market. The boatman tied the mooring rope, exhaled a stuffy breath, and busily jumped into the stern to make a fire and cook.

West Market is a small market town along the Mei River, located in the center between Song City and the county seat; the water journey from Song City would take two days, and West Market was exactly halfway; anchoring here for the night, he could reach the county seat in another day.

The depressed feeling of being cramped in the cabin all day also became as relaxed as the boatman putting down the bamboo pole on his shoulder.

Night greedily flowed down from the silent mountains; the river was a blur, with smoke and water indistinguishable. A row of dense tree shadows stretched along the embankment, covering the quiet, desolate market; the dark shadows of several boats floated sullenly under the embankment in front, the dim yellow lights of the boats reflected in the water, sifting into a swaying, soft fire snake. Under the black umbrella of night, West Market clearly lost its past bustle and prosperity.

Just as dinner was being prepared, someone on the embankment suddenly asked.

"Is that the boat of ××?"

The boat owner frowned, and hurriedly answered; just as he was about to step out, a lantern painted with red and black characters appeared at the bow, the dim yellow light revealed two guards with guns, and a middle-aged man dressed as a civil servant.

"Arriving so late, your——"

"Yes, yes, just arrived, sit in the cabin."

"No, no, your protection fee——"

"Ah, good, good…"

The boat owner answered while reaching into his belly pocket, fumbling for a while and then looking up at the civil servant-dressed man, with a smile on his face.

"Alas, it's really difficult, sir, you understand, things aren't like they used to be, I, I was thinking of paying half…"

"Tsk! You people are really——"

"No, it's not that I'm deliberately being difficult, it's just that…"

"I'm telling you, I'm handling official business, and it's all for the benefit of you boatmen, protecting you, it's not just for that one thing! You think, if you can pay half, everyone else will do the same, what will those dozens of brothers eat?"

After haggling for a while, the boat owner's hand was still in his belly pocket, which was a pity for the other side.

"Pay or not? Give me an answer! Who has time to dawdle with you!"

In the end, the power of the gun was terrifying, and ten shiny silver coins jumped from the boat owner's belly pocket into the other side's black leather bag.

"Protection, protection, protect your mother's ×! Always being ruthless on our heads! When the bandits' guns fire, you run and hide in your mother's ×!"

The boat owner who stepped back into the cabin had a flushed face.
