Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special Issue

Gary Cooper's Reasons for Movie Stars Fearing to Meet Journalists (Part 1)

— Ren Qin

Generally speaking, movie stars owe a great deal to film magazines and journalists for their success. If they didn't have so many magazines and journalists promoting them, nine out of ten times doing their duties for the reader's interests, their names would hardly be imprinted in the minds of the general public. Therefore, logically speaking, movie stars are usually very polite and respectful to journalists. However, some refuse to meet journalists, and some have to meet journalists but regard it as a difficult task. Gary Cooper is one such example.

It's not that Gary Cooper doesn't know the value of journalists and their publicity work, but he fears meeting them. He has many reasons. Now, to avoid misunderstandings, he has issued a statement. In it, he explains very thoroughly the reasons why movie stars in general fear meeting journalists. We will now translate it as a lesson for journalists, what do you think? The following is Gary Cooper's statement.

When we film actors show a little promise, many reporters from film magazines come to interview us. At that point, these magazines and writers are of great help to the fame of film professionals. Simply put, they create the star's fame. They first write a brief history of us, then how we entered the film industry, how we got good opportunities, and so on. After this material has been repeatedly used, they begin to write about our daily lives and other matters.

It is at this point that film actors begin to fear these journalists. They gradually begin to involve themselves in our personal private lives. They publish things we don't want published. They speculate non-consensually about things that are not the public's business and publish them to the masses. In the end, we have to adopt a strategy of self-defense, which is to avoid meeting journalists.

However, when we first announce that we will not meet journalists, we are immediately labeled as "stuck-up" or "arrogant." As for why we don't want to meet journalists, they ignore it. They also don't think about their unreasonable treatment of film actors, and that kind of publicity is worse than no publicity at all. They even say that movie stars are ungrateful. They think about how, when we first arrived in Hollywood, we liked to see them, afraid that they wouldn't come; but now that we're rich, we don't need them, so we don't see them, and so on. In fact, these are all misunderstandings.

When we don't receive journalists, we can't draw up a list of who is okay and who is not. Therefore, we can only refuse to see everyone. This, in turn, angers all the reporters. So some people start attacking you and saying bad things about you. Everyone sees those attacking words, some suspect that we have really changed, and many who originally liked us gradually become indifferent. I have suffered all the hardships mentioned above, and I must express my personal attitude.

I think my life is very ordinary and monotonous. I don't have any interesting anecdotes to tell people. But what journalists are looking for are special stories. If they published that I get up at seven in the morning when I'm working; get up at ten in the morning when I'm not working; have breakfast and go to the company; work until late; and then go home and not go out. Then people would think, this person is too ordinary and boring, and some people would say, what's the point of writing this kind of story? So, if journalists want to write about my daily life, they can't write about my real daily life, and they have to "invent" and "create."

When I was not married, I couldn't help but sometimes go out with girlfriends, it is impossible for a man to marry every woman he has ever gone out with. But it is also extremely rare for a man to only go out with one woman in his life. But every time I went out with a woman, the gossip column in the newspapers and magazines immediately recorded it.

That wouldn't be too bad, if they didn't add comments or speculations. But what I read often says: "Gary Cooper and Iris Macon were at such and such place last night. Iris is Gary's latest lover, but Gary is unpredictable, will Iris have the ability to catch him?" When you read this news, don't you think it's annoying? The next day, when I call Iris, you can imagine how I feel. I nervously wonder if Iris has seen the news…will she be angry…will she suspect that I have any intentions.

If I'm not too difficult, a lot of journalists will come to see me in a day or two. After talking about a lot of irrelevant things, they can't help but mention Iris's name. They ask me if Iris is a good person? Of course, she's good, otherwise I wouldn't go out with her. The second question is, do I want to marry her? How am I supposed to answer that? (To be continued)

Audience Opinions

Returning to "My Review"

— Mao Di

"Return," appearing in a new guise of "Three Modern Women," must be considered a progressive work among outdated films. From the point of view of the subject matter, although it is still the old stuff that has been repeatedly described, such as unemployment, disasters, and some of the love and abandonment that should exist in cities, these are precisely the common facts in today's society, and tragic scenes are unfolding frantically in both rural and urban areas. Unfortunately, the director's skills are too weak, and he cannot express these things deeply, only superficially explaining the accidental phenomenon, and it can be said that he has only introduced a few people playing together.

Moreover, the director's allocation of film for these three protagonists is uneven and unreasonable. I think at least he should write more about the elder sister who has a clear mind for independent living, but now most of the drama seems to be doing a mediocre biography for an unsound romantic girl, so that in the audience's impression, they feel that this woman who struggled out of the old forces is a superfluous character. Even that clear-headed elder sister was almost misunderstood in some places, and this can be attributed to the director's inability to arrange the script well.

The theme of this film is not so much to indicate the right path for women's lives as it is to praise the creative power of mankind to overcome the natural environment. In this respect, the picture does not have sufficient characteristics.

The tone of the whole drama is always on the horizontal line from beginning to end, and there is no climax that suddenly stimulates people, a film without a climax may make people doze off.

There are many flaws in this film, but there are also things worth mentioning. The suicide scene is quite skillful, and the three songs sung in the ballroom are inserted naturally.

The actors all worked hard, but Fan Xuepeng and Lu Lixia, one pretended not to be like, the other did not reach home; Chen Yan was still good. (Missing section)

After Seeing "Human Relations"

— Zhang Zhen

"Human Relations" is a new masterpiece by the Star Film Company after "Raging Current," with its new style and correct consciousness, it exposes the cruel reality of the current unbalanced socio-economic system in its entirety, using an objective and serious attitude to face it squarely, this is indeed the success of the playwright, but what is regrettable is that the exposure is still not enough.

"Human Relations" describes a hardworking dock worker, whose son is injured in a fire, and because of economic difficulties, medical treatment is refused. Therefore, Yu San (played by Jia Nong) wants to go astray to find a way out, but as a result, he is sanctioned by the law and imprisoned. After being released from prison, his wife has married Lu Daxiong, and his son also works in his bank. Yu San begins his wandering life on the road, and is later introduced by his gambling friend Yu Ming to work as his son's servant. In the end, Yu Ming's conspiracy breaks out, and Yu San dies under the bullets of the police while saving his son.

Anyone cannot deny Gong Jia Nong's efforts. His success is that he can work hard. We can still recall our past impression of him in "Raging Current." This time, with his realistic makeup and profound inner expressions, compared to all his previous films, it can be regarded as the most successful.

In addition to Gong Jia Nong, there is also a new person in "Human Relations"—Yuan Shaomei (playing Yu Lin's mother). It is rare for him to be able to play three different roles in the first time on the screen.

Regarding the photography aspect, of course, there are some places that cannot satisfy people. But Mr. Chen is also a new figure, and it is very gratifying that he has such achievements. The light is still good, but some places are unclear, but it is not a big problem. (Missing section)

A GlimPSE OF DIAN TONG'S GLORY

1. Zhou Boxun is in contact with various parties for location shooting of "The Goddess of Liberty," and already went to Hangzhou last Sunday. Situ Huimin, Wang Ying, and Zhang Yunqiao took the early train this morning from Shanghai to Hangzhou. As for the cameras, props, and staff, they are traveling in a Dian Tong truck, which is the third batch of people.

2. In "Sons and Daughters in a Time of Storm," there was a kissing scene between Tan Ying and Yuan Muzhi, which had already been filmed, but director Xu Xingzhi, in pursuit of perfection, disregarding Tan Ying's shyness, tried it three more times. Although this was difficult for Tan Ying, "Our Poet" Yuan Muzhi won three times in a row and had great romantic luck.

3. The lead actress for Dian Tong's fourth sound film, "Metropolitan Scenery," is being recruited through public advertisement in order to implement the original intention of using new talent. The number of applicants has been exceptionally high in recent days, and Dian Tong will unintentionally discover a new talent again.

4. With continuous spring rain, puddles of water have formed on Dian Tong's cement basketball court. The basketball players, feeling stifled by the weather, have all flocked to the ping pong room, immediately creating a vibrant atmosphere.

WU CUN AND "FALLING BLOSSOMS"

— You Guang

Wu Cun has received good praise in the Chinese film scene for his film "Remarriage."

His technique is light, the scenes are beautiful, and every foot of film is deeply imbued with poetry.

From the poetic title "Falling Blossoms," it is easy to imagine that this must be a sentimental and melancholic love story, but in reality, its theme is anti-imperialist. It depicts a group of righteous volunteers who, due to insufficient food and ammunition, have retreated and wandered into a big city. They shake off the coercion of hunger with tenacity, never becoming discouraged; they love to joke and make trouble, and have even suffered from women, but when the war breaks out again, they stand on the same front line.

The film is written and directed by Wu Cun, and the leading actors include Shen Lai, Sui Nong, Zhao Dan, Wang Xianqi, Gu Meijun, Gu Lanjun, etc. (Actually)

Film Novel

CLOUD SKY HATE BARRIER (LIVING ON VELVET) (4)

— Ti Yun

It was already two o'clock in the morning, and the two of them were still wandering outside without going home. At this time, they were eating beef pies in a food truck. The food vendor was not excited about having business. He felt that these high-class men and women did not even know when to close up shop, which was really annoying. But he couldn't bring himself to drive them away. So he said, "It's a good morning today." Thore didn't understand what he meant and retorted, "It looks like it's going to rain." The truck owner said again, "But the forecast in the newspaper is for sunny and warm weather." Thore said, "Then let's pray for rain." Amy also said, "I like rain." Saying that, the two of them still refused to leave. The truck owner had no choice but to let them be.

After a while, Thore seemed to realize something and exclaimed, "Oh, a joke, we haven't even exchanged names yet!" Amy said, "I've known your name for a long time. You're Thore Parker. I knew it as soon as I saw you because Walter mentioned you to me." Thore, upon hearing this, jumped up and said, "Then who are you?" Amy asked strangely, "Aren't I Amy? Don't you know?"

Thore, upon hearing this, seemed to have lost something, and his spirits immediately drooped. After a while, he muttered to himself. ( ) Of course, you are Amy... Walter's Amy... Amy said, "Just Amy is fine." Thore continued to mutter to himself, "There's a street lamp on Fifth Avenue, a leaf in Central Park, and a woman in New York. Millions of lamps, millions of women, but you just happen to be Walter's Amy." Amy said, "I'm not anyone's Walter or anything." Thore said, "But he loves you." Amy said, "Not that much." Thore said, "Of course you love him too." Amy said, "I don't see it that way either."

The two of them then stood up and went home. They didn't say much on the way. When Thore took Amy home, the guests had already left, but Walter hadn't left yet. Amy saw Walter and walked up to him, patting his shoulder and saying, "I know we shouldn't have left. Please forgive me." Thore stood aside, watching the two of them coldly, and couldn't help but say, "What a pair of lovers!" Then he said goodnight to them and quietly walked away alone.

The next day, Amy was sitting alone at home. She didn't eat anything all day. All she thought about was Thore... his expression when he left last night had been indelibly imprinted in her mind. After dinner, Walter came. Amy greeted him with infinite hope in her heart, but Walter shook his head slightly at her. Amy was holding a cigarette in her hand, but hadn't lit it. She unconsciously tore the cigarette paper to shreds. She said suddenly, "You must find him... do you understand? If you don't find him, don't come back..." Walter said, "I understand... I'll go again..."

Amy reached out her hand and shook his, saying, "I'm really sorry for you..." Walter said, "It's nothing. You love him, I know. As long as you're happy, I'm happy too." Upon hearing this, Amy's tears were about to burst out of her eyes, but she held back her tears and said, "You are the most righteous person in the world. You will find him, won't you?" Walter said, "That's right, I'll go guide him back."

Walter was a really good person. He soon found Thore and brought him home. Thore was taking a bath, and Amy had already received the news and rushed over, unable to wait even a minute. She met Thore in the bathroom, and they not only met but also got engaged. Regardless of her aunt Martha's protests, she married Thore in a church ceremony, and Walter was their only witness. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Automotive Weekly

INCREASE IN US AUTOMOBILE PRODUCTION CAPACITY

— Yu

ON PAR WITH PEAK YEARS

The American automobile manufacturing industry has recently shown a vigorous surge forward. According to Reuters, the March automobile production in the United States this year will be similar to the production of four years and nine months ago. Since May 1930, that is, fifty-seven months ago, the production of automobiles and freight trucks has never reached the number of 400,000 units. According to observers, this March, the automobile production will not only be the same as the level mentioned above, but will also exceed it. Therefore, it seems that the average total production per week in March will be around 100,000 units. The week has just ended, and the production volume has not yet been calculated. However, in fact, it is allowed to be the first time since the five-day work week became legal that the number has been reached.

Regardless of the month, if automobile production exceeds the number of 400,000 units, then statisticians consider it to be beyond normal. In 1930, there were only three such months: March, April, and May. 1929 was generally considered the prosperous year for the automotive industry. There were nine such months that year. There were eight in 1928, only three in 1927, six in 1926, and in 1925, automobile production reached approximately 4 million units, with five months exceeding the number.

When the production capacity of each automobile factory returns to 100,000 units per week, the heads of each factory plan a very careful step to avoid the hardships caused by overproduction in the past from reappearing today. At present, everyone believes that among all industries, the automobile manufacturing industry can be called a pillar of support. Major manufacturers are gradually increasing production, and according to reports from various sources, retail sales are also rising. However, in view of the instability in the market, such as the decline in stock market prices, the factory is also very careful and prudent. Other reasons for the factory's caution are the chaotic situation abroad, the obvious decline in the market for products, and the uncertain future of the recovery policy, all of which cause the executives of the factory to have concerns.

Engineers who plan and manufacture new types of automobiles are very puzzled by the fact that vehicle traffic accidents seem to be trending towards similar patterns. The occurrence of such accidents is unavoidable even for those with driving experience. In fact, investigations have shown that many experienced drivers are among the victims of these accidents. It is generally believed that the occurrence of such events is mostly due to drivers taking the mechanical structure of the automobile too lightly, unaware that the automobile they are driving is completely different from the ones they were used to seven or eight years ago. Today's automobiles have constantly increasing engine power and speed compared to those of seven or eight years ago. The brakes and other safety equipment are all extremely commensurate. It is a pity that the shortcomings of our minds cannot be managed by automobile engineers. Those who are negligent in this regard often cause great disasters and even lose their lives. It is estimated that between 1927 and 1934, the average horsepower of brakes increased from 65.8 horsepower to 112.5 horsepower. The situation is slightly different this year, with a slight drop to 109.6 horsepower.

The Indiana branch of the Society of Automotive Engineers recently held a meeting. The engineer Li Waierte Feiershi in that city raised a question for discussion. His idea was that the new cars of 1934 and 1935 have increased a lot of power, have no vibrations, and are very quiet, but in terms of accidents, he was afraid that there would be no decrease, but rather an increase. Drivers who are used to driving old-style cars will inevitably encounter difficulties when they change to new ones. In addition, because of the stability of the action, and the increase in power to the maximum limit, they are unaware of it and do not pay attention to the speedometer, turning the car at high speed. Moreover, after testing, it was found that when the car turns too fast, it is like a flash of lightning, not knowing whether the weight of the car body is balanced or not. By the time they realize it, it is too late, etc.

TALKING ABOUT THE HEAT SUPPLY OF THE CARBURETOR SYSTEM

— Lu

Any liquid, to make it evaporate into a gas, must be given considerable heat. The carburetor system of an automobile is also the same. As far as the gasoline sold on the market for automobiles is concerned, only a very small part of it can evaporate in ordinary atmospheric temperature. Even in hot summer weather, this is the case. In ordinary gasoline, in addition to this very small portion that is easy to evaporate, the rest, if it contains the heaviest molecules, has a boiling point that can reach as high as 450 degrees Fahrenheit. Therefore, in order to obtain proper evaporation and suitable spraying of gasoline to save fuel, the gasoline must be given considerable heat. Usually, this heat is applied after the gasoline has already evaporated.

In the past, the gasoline contained more easily evaporating molecules than difficult-to-evaporate molecules, so this kind of gasoline could be used anywhere. This kind of gasoline first heats the air before it enters the carburetor, then jackets the mixing chamber of the carburetor with a water jacket, and also jackets the intake pipe with a water jacket. After that, letting the water from the engine cooling system circulate in this water jacket can achieve the most satisfactory results. The water in this water jacket usually exceeds 170 degrees Fahrenheit. Such a low temperature is not suitable for evaporating the gasoline that contains more difficult-to-evaporate molecules now. That being said, this method of heating with a water jacket is a much greater improvement than the carburetors of the past that had no heating equipment at all.

As for heating the gasoline when it is still a liquid, the effect is also very good because the evaporation of the lighter molecules in the gasoline can be greatly helped by this, and the fuel is more economical. What is even more ideal is that in automobiles that are supplied with oil by vacuum tanks, in order to make the gasoline in the tank warm by the heat emitted by the engine cylinders, the position of the vacuum tank must be as close to the engine and carburetor as possible. Regarding the heating of liquid gasoline, this problem has been tested. The gasoline in the carburetor float chamber was heated by using a heating coil through which current supplied by a storage battery passed. As a result, it proved to be very successful for starting a cold engine. There are now several carburetors that have installed this type of electric primer. However, this type of heating equipment can only be used for starting the engine because it requires a very large amount of electricity. If used continuously, the current in the battery will be used up in a short time. (To be continued)

HUDSON AND TERRAPLANE UNIFORMLY ADOPT DOUBLE-FLOW LUBRICATION SYSTEM

— Yun

Regarding the various inspection works on automobile engines, the ones adopted by the Hudson Mechanical Engineering Department should be considered the most rigorous and difficult. This is uniformly praised by the city of Detroit and generally recognized by the public. Not long ago, a 1935 Terrapin engine completed a 208-hour test. In this test, the engine speed used was equal to 84 miles per hour. If this engine were installed in a car, its mileage could reach 17,472 miles in nine days. In other words, at a speed of 84 miles per hour, without stopping or slowing down, it could cross America six times. According to the Hudson engineers, this type of test is of great importance to the lubrication system. In this test, each piston stroke was equal to 7,878 miles, the camshaft rotated 24,960,000 times, and the crankshaft rotated 49,920,000 times. The endurance movements of the other parts were also commendable. However, even after this arduous work, there was absolutely no impact or damage to any part of the engine when it was disassembled. Also, the lower end bearing of the connecting rod was at the forefront of this type of test, but as a result, the average degree of wear was less than three ten-thousandths of an inch. As for the pistons, they were undamaged, and all the bearing surfaces on the piston pins were also as good as new. All of this is due to the perfect lubrication system that made it so. The lubrication system used is a double-flow type, which uses a double-acting reciprocating pump to distribute the oil through both ends of the crankshaft and through the guide pipes to the oil tank, where it is collected from the lower end of the connecting rod to apply oil to all necessary parts with great pressure. The excellent operating performance of the Hudson and Terrapin engines is one of the characteristics of this lubrication system. Once the engine is started, the oil is immediately transmitted to all moving parts. This alone is one of the outstanding advantages of the Hudson double-flow lubrication system that is far beyond reach.

THE SO-CALLED "F.O.B." PRICE OF US AUTOMOBILE FACTORIES

The so-called "F.O.B." (Free On Board) Factory Price of a car from an American automobile factory is 850 yuan.

In fact, you cannot buy this car at this price. In the United States, if the "F.O.B." price of a car is 1,000 yuan or less, the delivered price is often about 25% higher than the "F.O.B." price. Assuming there is a more expensive car with a "F.O.B." price of 1,026 yuan, then you have to pay 1,173 yuan in New York to buy it, which is an increase of about 14%.

Automobile industries in various countries, if they want to compare the "F.O.B." price of American cars with the delivered price, should remember the facts mentioned above, and should pay attention to automobile retailers or salesmen. If they use the pricing of American automobiles to undermine their competitors, do not be deceived by them, because the pricing of American automobiles is specifically for an empty car, without bumpers or spare tires, which are essential parts of the car. Other parts that are indispensable in the current situation are also missing.

The equipment included in the "F.O.B." price of American automobiles varies depending on the brand. Generally, safety glass, front and rear insurance bumpers, clocks, spare tires, double tail lights, and double horns are not included. In fact, no one in the United States can buy a car at the list price. Not to mention overseas countries, which have to add transportation, tax, insurance, and other fees.

Occasionally, an American runs to an automobile factory and asks to buy a car at the list price, but he inevitably pays some tips, and he also has to bring a letter of introduction and say many moral good words before he can drive the car away. All the essential safety equipment can be properly equipped.

The pricing of American automobiles was originally just a basis for accounting, used to indicate the category to which each car should be classified, and not the actual price of each car. However, just because of this pricing, many doubts have arisen in the overseas automotive industry after seeing it in various magazines and publications.

ABOVE IS A VIEW OF THE SPACIOUS SEATS OF A 1935 BRITISH STANDARD CAR

Page 26

Doubts have arisen, and it is inevitable that criticism will be directed at automobile import firms because the so-called pricing in the United States is clearly inconsistent with the selling price overseas.

It should be known that the price paid by Americans for cars is indeed lower than the price paid overseas, but this is not due to the fault of the factory, nor is it due to the fault of the import firm. Part of the reason lies in the special needs of export trade, and part of the reason lies in the additional costs of packaging, transportation, and taxes, among which taxes are the largest.

Many American automobile factories often go the extra mile for export cars, such as equipping special steering knuckles and springs to adapt to the road conditions in overseas markets.

Since transportation and taxes are added to the list price, its overseas price will be twice the price in the United States, or even more. However, import firms do not profit from this. Because the profit of importers is based on the total investment, not just the investment in automobiles. If importers only profit 25% on the price of automobiles and do not seek to profit from freight and taxes, then the result will only be a gross profit of 15%, and in reality, they will inevitably suffer losses.

A few years ago, a famous automobile factory changed its policy. The prices quoted were not "F.O.B." prices, but prices delivered to several major cities, and ultimately suffered a great failure.

However, the proposal for reform is now unanimously supported. Most export experts and domestic experts advocate thorough reform and abandoning the "F.O.B." price. Mr. Colin, the sales manager of a special factory, recently stated at the Detroit Transportation Association: "We don't want to say (you have 900 yuan to buy a car, but if you want a complete car, you have to pay 1,200 yuan), etc."

Many overseas distribution points also deeply resent and hate this system because it easily leads to misunderstandings. Car customers who do not use their brains occasionally see the price list in American magazines and immediately make a quick judgment, thinking that importers are asking for excessive prices and are deeply dissatisfied. For this reason, American exporters also want to plan reforms in order to save the situation.

Some advocate prohibiting the pricing of automobiles from being published in export publications. However, some exporters do not think so, because publication can prevent distribution points from seeking improper benefits. And even if exporters do not publish, other publications will publish it, so prohibition is useless.

The most important method is to make the overseas automotive industry thoroughly understand the American "F.O.B." price. It should be known that this price is just a basis. From this basis, the actual price that the car owner has to pay can be calculated, and the category of various prices can be expressed.
